DIVISION 2. - BOARD OF REGISTRARS[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
State Law reference- Registration of voters, O.C.G.A. § 21-2-210 et seq.

Sec. 2-71. - Established; composition. 
    There is hereby established a board of registrars for the city. It shall consist of a chief registrar and five (5) regular members to be appointed by the board of commissioners. 
(Ord. of 9-30-75B, § 1)
Sec. 2-72. - Terms of members. 
    Such members of the board of registrars as may be appointed shall serve at the pleasure of the board of commissioners for staggered terms as follows: 
One (1) member for a one-year term; 
Two (2) members for two-year terms; 
Two (2) members for three-year terms. 
(Ord. of 9-30-75B, § 2)
Sec. 2-73. - Member eligibility. 
(a)	For a person to be eligible to serve on the board of registrars, he must:
(1)	Be an elector of the city;
(2)	Be able to read, write and speak the English language.
(b)	No person, while serving as registrar or within a period of six (6) months after so serving, shall be eligible to any nomination or elective office of the city to be voted for at a primary or election. 
(c)	Each registrar shall take an oath of office before entering upon his duties, administered by the city clerk. 
(Ord. of 9-30-75B, § 3)
Sec. 2-74. - Duties of chief registrar. 
    The chief registrar shall have the following duties: 
(1)	Serve as the chief administrative officer of the board of registrars and generally supervise and direct the administration of the affairs of the board of registrars; 
(2)	Register electors qualified to vote;
(3)	Take applications of prospective electors to vote;
(4)	Keep and preserve a voter registration list for municipal elections as certified to by the board, designating those persons who are qualified electors for the city. 
(Ord. of 9-30-75B, § 4)
Sec. 2-75. - Duties of board. 
    The board of registrars shall have the following duties: 
(1)	Prepare for use in all city primaries and elections a true and correct list of the electors of the city, placing thereon only those persons found to be qualified to vote; 
(2)	Examine from time to time the qualifications of each elector who is registered to vote and whose name is entered upon the list of electors, and purge from such registration those not qualified to vote in municipal primaries and elections; 
(3)	Challenge those electors whose qualifications are questioned by the board, but only after first giving notice in writing to the listed elector of such challenge with an opportunity to be heard on the right to remain on the list; 
(4)	Conduct hearings open to the public on the right of a person to be registered as an elector and to appear on the list of electors eligible to vote and decide the question of eligibility and qualification of electors in the event of challenge by the board or any other person; 
(5)	File with the city clerk at least three (3) days prior to any primary or election a certified copy of a list containing the names of all the electors found to be qualified to vote in the upcoming primary or election. 
(Ord. of 9-30-75B, § 5)
Sec. 2-76. - Compliance with state law. 
    The board of registrars established by this division shall be bound by the state laws governing municipal elections in carrying out its duties and in particular it shall follow those rules set forth for registration of voters in O.C.G.A. tit. 21, ch. 2, art. VI § 21-2-210 et seq.). 
(Ord. of 9-30-75B, § 6)
Secs. 2-77-2-95. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - RECREATION COMMISSION[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
State Law reference- County's and municipality's power to provide parks, recreation areas, programs and facilities, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(5); city's authority to construct and operate parks, swimming pools, golf courses, recreation grounds and buildings used for sports, O.C.G.A. § 36-34-3; establishment of recreation systems, O.C.G.A. § 36-64-1 et seq.

Sec. 2-96. - Established; membership; term; vacancies; removal. 
(a)	Under the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 36-64-4, a joint city-county recreation commission was established and provided for by the city concurrent with the action of the commissioner of roads and revenues of the county. 
(b)	The joint commission shall be a board of nine (9) persons serving without pay, five (5) of whom shall be appointed by the county and four (4) of whom shall be appointed by the city. 
(c)	The initial term of the commissioners appointed by the city shall be as follows: Post 1 shall expire July 13, 2015, Post 2 shall expire July 13, 2016, Post 3 shall expire July 13, 2017 and Post 4 shall expire July 13, 2018. Thereafter, the term of office of such commissioners appointed shall be for five (5) years. 
(d)	Vacancies in the commission occurring otherwise then by expiration of terms shall be filled by another appointment for the unexpired term of that member either by the county or the city. 
(e)	Any member of the recreation commission can be removed by majority vote of the city commission. Absence from two (2) meetings within a calendar year without justification may be cause for removal from the commission. 
(Ord. No. 2013-4, 9-9-13)
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2013-4, adopted Sept. 9, 2013, deleted § 2-96, in its entirety and enacted new provisions to read as herein set out. Prior to this amendment § 2-96 pertained to "Established, membership." See Code Comparative Table for derivation. 
Sec. 2-97. - Organizational meeting; rules. 
    Immediately after its appointment, the recreation commission shall meet and organize by electing one (1) of its members president and such other officers as may be necessary. The commission shall have power to adopt bylaws, rules and regulations for the proper conduct of recreation for the city and county. 
(Code 1969, § 12-2)
Sec. 2-98. - Function. 
    The recreation commission shall provide, conduct and supervise public playgrounds, playfields, indoor recreation centers and other recreation facilities owned or controlled by the city or county or both. It shall have the power to conduct any form of recreation or cultural activity that will employ the leisure time of the people in a wholesome and constructive manner. It may conduct such activities on properties under its own control, on public properties with the consent of the authorities thereof, and on private property with the consent of the owners. 
(Code 1969, § 12-3)
Sec. 2-99. - Appointment of superintendent, other personnel. 
    The recreation commission shall have the power to appoint or designate someone to act as superintendent, who is trained or properly qualified for the work, and such other personnel as the commission deems proper. 
(Code 1969, § 12-4)
Sec. 2-100. - Finances. 
    Annually the recreation commission shall submit a budget to the governing body of both the city and county for its approval. The commission may also solicit or receive any gifts or bequests of money or other personal property or any donation to be applied, principal or income, for either temporary or permanent use of playgrounds or other recreational purposes. The city and county shall divide the budget pro rata in accordance with a formula mutually agreeable to both governing bodies. 
(Code 1969, § 12-5)
Sec. 2-101. - Reports. 
    The recreation commission shall make an annual report to the governing body of each authority and such other reports as from time to time may be requested by either. 
(Code 1969, § 12-6)
Secs. 2-102-2-110. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - CODE OF ETHICS[6] 

Footnotes: 
--- (6) --- 
Editor's note-An Ordinance of Jan. 5, 2000, enacted provisions to establish a new chapter 20 to include §§ 20-1-20-11. To maintain alphabetical sequence of the Code, said ordinance was set out as article V, §§ 2-111-2-121 at the editor's discretion.
State Law reference- Public ethics, O.C.G.A. § 45-10-1.

Sec. 2-111. - Declaration of policy. 
(a)	Those who are elected to serve the public as representatives accept a public trust, which they share with those whom they elect, appoint, hire, or otherwise enlist to help them serve the public. The public entrusts its power and resources to its servants to use only in the public interest. Public trust requires public servants to fulfill their public duties faithfully and honestly, and to subordinate any personal interest which conflicts with the public interest. Public trust also requires that acts which are contrary to the public interest be defined and prohibited; that there be an orderly procedure for raising and addressing ethical questions; that ethical behavior be encouraged and suitably rewarded; that unethical behavior be discouraged and suitably disciplined through a process which is fundamentally fair. 
(b)	It is the responsibility of each public servant to act in a manner which contributes to cultivating public trust in the integrity of government. Public trust in the integrity of government is cultivated when individual public servants act with integrity and when the public is aware that its servants act with integrity. 
(Ord. of 1-5-00)
Sec. 2-112. - Purposes of article. 
    This article is adopted: 
(1)	To state principles of ethics which are to be applied in public service;
(2)	To identify minimum standards of ethical conduct for public servants;
(3)	To require the public servants to engage in ethical practices which always meet minimum standards; 
(4)	To encourage public servants to pursue the highest ethical ideals which they can achieve;
(5)	To provide a process by which public service may identify and resolve ethical issues;
(6)	To inform public servants and the public of the minimum standards to which public servants must adhere; 
(7)	To promote public confidence in the integrity of public servants;
(8)	To encourage members of the public to seek public office or employment, to serve on public boards, to assist public servants as volunteers, and to take pride in participating in the governmental process; 
(9)	To establish penalties, as appropriate, for public servants who violate the public trust; and 
(10)	To provide for a just and reasonable balance among the rights of all individuals who are directly affected by the operation of this article. 
(Ord. of 1-5-00)
Sec. 2-113. - Scope of persons covered. 
    The provision of this Code of Ethics shall be applicable to all members of the board of commissioners of the City of Hawkinsville, the planning and zoning commission of the City of Hawkinsville, appointed committees, advisory commissions and committee members and city officials. 
(Ord. of 1-5-00)
Sec. 2-114. - Definitions. 
    As used in this article, the following terms shall have the following meanings, unless the context clearly indicates a different meaning is intended: 
    City official or official, unless otherwise expressly defined, means the board of commissioners of the City of Hawkinsville, individually and collectively; municipal court judges, city manager; finance officer; assistant city manager; city clerk, deputy city clerk, whether such person is salaried, hired, or elected, and all other persons holding positions designated by the City Charter or hired with the board of commissioners and includes individuals appointed by the chairman and board of commissioners to all city commissions, committees, boards, task forces or other city bodies unless specifically exempted from this article by the board of commissioners. 
    Entity means that a sole proprietorship, partnership, limited partnership, firm, corporation, professional corporation, holding company, joint stock company, receivership, trust or any other entity recognized by law through which business may be conducted. 
    Decision means any ordinance, resolution, contract, franchise, formal action or other matter voted on by the board of commissioners or other city board or commission. 
    Discretionary authority means the power to exercise any judgment in a decision or action. 
    Immediate family means spouse, mother, father, brother, sister, son or daughter of any city official. 
    Remote interest means any interest of a person or entity, including a city official, that affects this person, entity or city official in the same way as the general public is affected. 
    Interest means any direct pecuniary benefit, which is not a remote interest. A city official or official shall be deemed to have an interest in transactions involving: 
(1)	Any person, city official's immediate family;
(2)	Any person with whom a contractual relationship exists whereby the city official will receive any payment or other benefits unless the city official is receiving a benefit for goods or services in the normal course of business for which the city official has paid a commercially reasonable rate; 
(3)	Any entity in which the city official is a director, officer, employee, agent, or shareholder unless otherwise provided herein; or 
(4)	Any person to whom the city official is a creditor, whether secured or unsecured.
    Complaint means a written sworn statement filed with the city manager of the City of Hawkinsville containing specific allegations of misconduct by an official; provided, however, such allegations must be filed within thirty (30) days of discovery of the alleged misconduct. 
(Ord. of 1-5-00)
Sec. 2-115. - Prohibitions. 
    No city official shall: 
(1)	Fail to uphold the Constitution, Laws and Regulations of the United States, the State of Georgia, and the City of Hawkinsville; 
(2)	Discriminate by the dispensing of special favors or privileges to anyone, whether or not for remuneration; 
(3)	Engage in any business with the City of Hawkinsville, either directly or indirectly, which is inconsistent with the conscientious performance of the city official's governmental duties; 
(4)	Use any information given to him or her confidentially in the performance of governmental duties as a means of making private profit; 
(5)	Fail to expose corruption wherever discovered;
(6)	Solicit, accept or agree to accept gifts, loans, gratuities, discounts, favors, hospitality or services from any person, association or corporation under circumstances from which it could reasonably be inferred that a major purpose of the donor is to influence the performance of the city official's governmental duties; 
(7)	Accept any economic opportunity under circumstances where he or she knows or should know that there is a substantial possibility that the opportunity is being afforded him or her with intent to influence his or her conduct in the performance of official duties; 
(8)	Take any official action with regard to any matter under circumstances in which he or she knows or should know that he or she has a direct or indirect monetary interest in the subject matter of such matter or in the outcome of such official action; 
(9)	Engage in, accept employment with, or render services for any private business or professional activity when such employment or rendering of services is adverse to and incompatible with the proper discharge of official duties; 
(10)	Engage in any activity or transaction as prohibited by law now existing or hereinafter enacted which is applicable to him or her by virtue of being an official of the City of Hawkinsville; 
(11)	Use his or her position to request or require an employee of the City of Hawkinsville to: 
a.	Do clerical work on behalf of the member's family, business, social, church or fraternal interest when such work is not furthering a city interest; 
b.	Perform any work outside the employee's normal course of municipal employment;
c.	Purchase goods or services to be used for personal, business or political purposes;
d.	Work for the member personally without paying the employee just compensation;
(12)	To use property of the City of Hawkinsville of any kind for other than officially approved activities; 
(13)	Any official who has a proprietary interest in any entity doing business with the city shall make known that interest; 
(14)	Participate in a vote or decision on a matter affecting a person, entity, or property in which the official has an interest. 
Prohibition (2) of this section shall not apply in the case of: 
a.	An occasional non-pecuniary gift of insignificant value;
b.	An award publicly presented in recognition of public service;
c.	A commercially reasonable loan or other financial transaction made in the ordinary course of business by an institution or individual authorized by the laws of Georgia to engage in the making of such a loan or financial transaction; 
d.	Campaign contributions made and reported in accordance with Georgia Law.
(Ord. of 1-5-00)
Sec. 2-116. - Disclosure of conflicts of interest. 
    An official of the City of Hawkinsville who has an interest that he/she has reason to believe may be affected by his/her official acts or actions or by the official acts or actions of the board of commissioners shall disclose the precise nature of such interest prior to the board of commissioners taking official action on a matter affecting such interest and shall abstain from discussion or voting. The disclosure of such interest shall be recorded into the minutes of the meeting and thus become a part of the public record. The official shall refrain from all ex-parte communications with other officials regarding the application in which he/she has an interest. 
(Ord. of 1-5-00)
Sec. 2-117. - Disqualification. 
    A member of the board of commissioners shall disqualify himself/herself from participating in any official act or action of the city which results in a pecuniary benefit to the official or a business or activity in which he/she has an interest, when such benefit is not available to the public at large. 
(Ord. of 1-5-00)
Sec. 2-118. - Prohibited contracts. 
(a)	The board of commissioners shall not enter into any contract involving services or property with an official or with a business in which an official has an interest. This section shall not apply to contracts entered into with an official, or with an entity in which an official has an interest, provided that such contract is the result of a competitive bid, and disclosure of the nature of such official's interest is made prior to the bids being opened and the interested official has disqualified himself/herself from participating in any official action with respect thereto. Further, this section shall not apply in the case of: 
(1)	The designation of a bank or trust company as a depository for funds of the City of Hawkinsville; 
(2)	Borrowing of funds from any bank or lending institution which offers the lowest available rate of interest; 
(3)	Contracts entered into in accordance with the Official Code of Georgia, Annotated, Section 16-10-6. 
(Ord. of 1-5-00)
Sec. 2-119. - Procedure upon receipt of complaint. 
(a)	Upon receipt of a complaint, the judge of the Municipal Court of the City of Hawkinsville shall appoint two (2) registered voters, who, along with the municipal court judge shall constitute the ethics committee. 
(b)	Upon receipt of a complaint in proper form, the ethics committee shall review it to determine whether the complaint is unjustified, frivolous, or patently unfounded, in which event such complaint shall be dismissed and the complainant notified immediately. 
(c)	In the event the complaint is found to state sufficient facts to warrant a hearing, the ethics committee is empowered to conduct probable cause investigation, to take evidence and hold hearings. 
(d)	In the event a complaint stating sufficient facts to warrant a hearing, the board shall hold a hearing within sixty (60) days after its initial review of the complaint. The failure of the ethics committee to hold a hearing within the specified time shall result in the dismissal of the complaint as to the matter complained of and shall prevent a re-filing if a complaint arises in the same matter for a period of six (6) months. 
(e)	The ethics committee shall provide its findings to the board of commissioners for such action as the board of commissioners deems appropriate. 
(f)	The ethics committee appointed herein shall cause the complaint to be served on the city official charged as soon as practical. Service may be by personal service or by certified mail, return receipt requested. The hearing shall be held within sixty (60) days after filing of the complaint. The ethics committee shall conduct the hearing in accordance with the procedures and regulations it establishes but, in all circumstances, the hearing shall include the taking of testimony and the cross-examination of witnesses. The decision of the ethics committee shall be rendered to the board of commissioners within five (5) days after completion of the hearing. 
(Ord. of 1-5-00)
Sec. 2-120. - Penalty and city official rights. 
(a)	Any city official who violates any provision of this Code of Ethics as provided for in this article shall be subject to public reprimand or censure by the board of commissioners of the City of Hawkinsville. 
(b)	Any hearing held by the ethics committee, the city official who is the subject of inquiry, shall have the right to written notice of the allegations at least ten (10) business days before a hearing, to be represented by counsel, to hear and examine the evidence and witnesses in opposition or in extenuation. 
(Ord. of 1-5-00)
Sec. 2-121. - Appeals. 
(a)	Any city official adversely affected by the findings of the ethics committee may obtain judicial review of such decision as provided in this section. 
(b)	Action for judicial review may be commenced by filing an application for a writ of certiorari in the superior court of Pulaski County within thirty (30) days after application has been received from the ethics committee. The filing of such application shall act as supersedes. 
(Ord. of 1-5-00)
Secs. 2-122-2-130. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - CODE ENFORCEMENT BOARD 

Sec. 2-131. - Established, membership. 
(a)	Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 36-74-1, et seq., there is hereby established a code enforcement board. 
(b)	The board shall consist of five (5) members who shall be residents of the city.
(c)	The members of the board shall be appointed by the board of commissioners of the city for three-year terms. Provided, however, of the initial appointments, two (2) shall be appointed for a one-year term, two (2) shall be appointed for a two-year term, and two (2) shall be appointed for a three-year term. Thereafter, all members shall be appointed for three-year terms. 
(d)	Any member of the board may be reappointed upon approval of the commission.
(e)	An appointment to fill any vacancy on the code enforcement board shall be for the remainder of the unexpired term of office. If any member fails to attend two (2) of three (3) successive meetings without cause and without prior approval of the chairperson, the code enforcement board shall declare the member's office vacant, and the local governing body shall promptly fill such vacancy. 
(f)	Any board member may be suspended and removed for cause. The commission may, with or without cause, refuse to reappoint any member of the code enforcement board at the expiration of his or her term of office. 
(g)	The members of the code enforcement board shall elect a chairperson, who shall be a voting member, from among the members of the board. The presence of three (3) or more members shall constitute a quorum. Members of the board shall serve without compensation but may be reimbursed for such travel, mileage, and per diem expenses as may be authorized by the commission or as otherwise provided by law. 
(Ord. No. 2015-2, 6-1-2015) 
Sec. 2-132. - Enforcement proceedings. 
(a)	It shall be the duty of the city code enforcement official to initiate enforcement proceedings pursuant to the various codes adopted by the city; however, no member of the board shall have the power to initiate such enforcement proceedings. 
(b)	Except as provided in subsections c and d of this section, if a violation of any code or ordinance is found, the code inspector shall notify the violator and give him or her a reasonable time to correct the violation. Should the violation continue beyond the time specified for correction, the code enforcement official shall proceed through the code enforcement board. The code enforcement official should notify the enforcement board and request a hearing. The code enforcement board shall schedule a hearing and written notice of such hearing shall be hand delivered or made as provided in section 2-137. If the violation is corrected and then recurs or if the violation is not corrected by the time specified for correction by the code enforcement official, the case may be presented to the code enforcement board even if the violation has been corrected prior to the board hearing, and the notice shall so state. 
(c)	If a repeat violation is found, the code enforcement official shall notify the violator but is not required to give the violator a reasonable time to correct the violation. The code enforcement official, upon notifying the violator of a repeat violation, shall notify the code enforcement board and request a hearing. The code enforcement board shall schedule a hearing and shall provide written notice pursuant to section 2-137. The case may be presented to the enforcement board even if the repeat violation has been corrected prior to the board hearing, and the notice shall so state. 
(d)	If the code enforcement official has substantial reason to believe the violation presents a serious threat to the public health, safety and welfare or if the violation is irreparable or irreversible in nature, the code enforcement official shall make a reasonable effort to notify the violator and may immediately notify the code enforcement board and request a hearing. 
(Ord. No. 2015-2, 6-1-2015) 
Sec. 2-133. - Conduct of hearings. 
(a)	Upon request of the code enforcement official, or at such other times as may be necessary, the chairperson of the code enforcement board may call a hearing of the code enforcement board; a hearing also may be called by written notice signed by at least two (2) members of the board. Minutes shall be kept of all hearings by each code enforcement board, and all hearings and proceeding shall be open to the public. The commission may provide or assign clerical and administrative personnel to assist the code enforcement board in the proper performance of its duties. 
(b)	Each case before the code enforcement board shall be presented by the city attorney or by the code enforcement official or other member of the administrative staff of the commission. 
(c)	All testimony shall be under oath and shall be recorded. The code enforcement board shall take testimony from the code enforcement official and the alleged violator. Formal rules of evidence shall not apply, but fundamental due process shall be observed and shall govern the proceedings. 
(d)	At the conclusion of the hearing, the enforcement board shall issue findings of fact, based on evidence of record and conclusions of law, and shall issue an order affording the proper relief consistent with the powers contained in this article. The findings and conclusions shall be by motion approved by a majority of those members present and voting, except that at least three (3) members must vote in order for the action to be official. 
(Ord. No. 2015-2, 6-1-2015) 
Sec. 2-134. - Powers of code enforcement board. 
    The code enforcement board shall have the power to: 
(1)	Adopt rules for the conduct of its hearings, which rules shall, at a minimum, insure that each side has an equal opportunity to present evidence and argument in support of its case; 
(2)	Subpoena alleged violators and witnesses to its hearings. Subpoenas may be served by the sheriff department or by any other individual authorized by O.C.G.A. § 24-10-23 to serve subpoenas; 
(3)	Subpoena evidence to its hearings in the same way as provided in paragraph (2) of this section with the approval of the court with jurisdiction over a criminal violator of the municipal code. 
(4)	Take testimony under oath; and
(5)	Issue orders having the force of law to command whatever steps are necessary to bring a violation into compliance. 
(Ord. No. 2015-2, 6-1-2015) 
Sec. 2-135. - Administrative fines. 
(a)	The code enforcement board, upon notification by the code enforcement official that an order of the code enforcement board has not been complied with by the set time may order the violator to pay an administrative fine in an amount specified in this Code section. 
(b)	(1)	The administrative fine imposed pursuant to this code section for a violation involving the health or safety of a third party shall not exceed three hundred dollars ($300.00) per day. 
(2)	An administrative fine imposed by this code section for a violation that is not a violation involving the health or safety of a third party shall not exceed one hundred dollars ($100.00) per day. 
(3)	In determining the amount of the fine, if any, the code enforcement board shall consider the following factors: 
a.	The gravity of the violation;
b.	Any actions taken by the violator to correct the violation; and
c.	Any previous violations committed by the violator.
(3)	The code enforcement board may reduce a fine imposed pursuant to this Code section.
(c)	A certified copy of an order imposing an administrative fine may be recorded in the public records of any county and thereafter shall constitute a lien against the land on which the violation exists and upon any real or personal property owned by the violator. Upon petition to the Pulaski County Superior Court, such order may be enforced in the same manner as a court judgment by the sheriffs of this state, including a levy against the personal property, but such order shall not be deemed to be a court judgment except for enforcement purposes. After three (3) months from the filing of any such lien which remains unpaid, the code enforcement board may request the attorney for the city to foreclose the lien. 
(Ord. No. 2015-2, 6-1-2015) 
Sec. 2-136. - Appeals. 
    An aggrieved party, including the Commission of the City of Hawkinsville, may appeal a final administrative order of the code enforcement board to the Pulaski County Superior Court. Such an appeal shall be a hearing de novo. An appeal must be filed within thirty (30) days of the execution of the order to be appealed. 
(Ord. No. 2015-2, 6-1-2015) 
Sec. 2-137. - Notices. 
(a)	All notices required by this article shall be provided to the alleged violator by certified mail or statutory overnight delivery, return receipt requested; by hand delivery by the sheriff or other law enforcement officer, code enforcement official or other person designated by the commission of the City of Hawkinsville; or by leaving the notice at the violator's usual place of residence with any person residing therein who is above fifteen (15) years of age and informing such person of the contents of the notice. 
(b)	In addition to providing notice as set forth in subsection (a) of this section, at the option of the code enforcement board, notice may also be served by publication with notice published once during each week for four (4) consecutive weeks (four (4) publications being sufficient) in the newspaper in which sheriff's advertisements are printed in Pulaski County. Proof of publication shall be made by affidavit of a duly authorized representative of the newspaper. 
(Ord. No. 2015-2, 6-1-2015) 
Chapter 3 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Driving while under the influence of alcohol or drugs, § 11-2; drinking in public, § 11-9; taxation, licenses and business regulations, Ch. 16; zoning, Ch. 19.
State Law reference- Georgia Alcoholic Beverage Code, O.C.G.A. § 3-1-1 et seq.; public drunkenness, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-41; furnishing alcoholic beverages to persons under twenty-one years of age, jurisdiction of municipal courts, O.C.G.A. § 36-32-10; driving under the influence of alcohol or drugs, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-391.

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note-Ord. No. 2012-3, § 2, adopted Mar. 5, 2012, renumbered Ch. 3, Art. I, §§ 3-2-3-9 as Art. I, §§ 3-5-3-12. Section 3 of said ordinance enacted new provisions to read as Art. I, §§ 3-2-3-4. Prior to this amendment, Art. I pertained to similar subject matter. See Code Comparative Table for derivation.

Sec. 3-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms, and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Alcohol means ethyl alcohol, hydrated oxide of ethyl, or spirits of wine, from whatever source or by whatever process produced. 
    Alcoholic beverage means and includes all alcohol, distilled spirits, beer, malt beverage, wine, or fortified wine. 
    Church means any permanent building where persons regularly assemble for religious worship. 
    Distilled spirits means any alcoholic beverage obtained by distillation or containing more than twenty-one (21) percent alcohol by volume, including, but not limited to, all fortified wines. 
    Fortified wine means any alcoholic beverage containing more than twenty-one (21) percent alcohol by volume made from fruits, berries, or grapes either by natural fermentation or by natural fermentation with brandy added. The term includes, but is not limited to, brandy. 
    Gallon or wine gallon means a United States gallon of liquid measure equivalent to the volume of two hundred thirty-one (231) cubic inches or the nearest equivalent metric measurement. 
    Malt beverage means any alcoholic beverage obtained by the fermentation of any infusion or decoction of barley, malt, hops, or any other similar product, or any combination of such products in water, containing not more than six (6) percent alcohol by volume and including ale, porter, brown, stout, lager beer, small beer, and strong beer. The term does not include sake, known as Japanese rice wine. 
    Manager means the person in charge of the day-to-day operations of the business establishment for which application is being made. 
    Package means a bottle, can, keg, barrel, or other original consumer container. 
    Person means any individual, firm, partnership, cooperative, nonprofit membership corporation, joint venture, association, company, corporation, agency, syndicate, estate, trust, business trust, receiver, fiduciary, or other group or combination acting as a unit, body politic, or political subdivision, whether public, private, or quasipublic. 
    Premises means the definite closed or partitioned establishment, whether room, shop, or building wherein alcoholic beverages are sold or consumed. 
    Retail consumption dealer means any person who sells distilled spirits for consumption on the premises at retail only to consumers and not for resale. 
    Retailer or retail dealer means, except as to distilled spirits, any person who sells alcoholic beverages, either in unbroken packages or for consumption on the premises, at retail only to consumers and not for resale. With respect to distilled spirits, the term means any person who sells distilled spirits in unbroken packages at retail only to consumers and not for resale. 
    School property means property of state, county, city, or church schools and such other schools as teach subjects commonly taught in the common schools of this state, including playgrounds, athletic fields, tennis courts, and other instructional areas contiguous to such property which is used by any such schools for the purpose of teaching physical education, band, or other subjects which constitute a part of the school's curriculum. 
    Special event means any organized for profit activity having as its purpose entertainment, recreation, and/or education which takes place on public property or takes place on private property but requires special public services such as the use of parks, public streets, rights-of-ways, or sidewalks as well as events that take place in local business establishments that are outside of the "normal" course of business. Special events may include, but are not limited to, activities such as run/walk events, cycling events, street festivals, parades, grand openings, sales promotional events, concerts, assemblies, block parties and certain outdoor promotional events. 
    Wine means any alcoholic beverage containing not more than twenty-one (21) percent alcohol by volume made from fruits, berries, or grapes, either by natural fermentation or by natural fermentation with brandy added. The term includes, but is not limited to, all sparkling wines, champagnes, combinations of such beverages, vermouths, special natural wines, rectified wines, and like products. The term does not include cooking wine mixed with salt or other ingredients so as to render same unfit for human consumption as a beverage. A liquid shall first be deemed to be a wine at that point in the manufacturing process when it conforms to this definition. 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-1; Ord. No. 2006-3, 11-22-06; Ord. No. 2012-1, § 1, 1-9-12)
State Law reference- Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 3-1-2. 
Sec. 3-2. - Application. 
(a)	Generally. No license for the sale of alcoholic beverages at retail shall be granted until the application, accompanied by a check or cash in the amount required for the license, setting forth the name of the owners, the business and its location, shall have been approved by the sheriff, the fire chief and the building inspector. The department directors shall file a written recommendation for approval or denial with the clerk within thirty (30) days from the filing date. A recommendation for denial shall set forth the specific reasons thereof. If the department directors are unable to complete the investigation and make their recommendation within the time prescribed, a written statement setting forth reasons for the delay shall be filed with the clerk. As soon as the reasons for delay have ceased to exist, the investigation shall be completed and the recommendation shall be filed with the clerk. Upon receipt of the recommendation, the clerk will present it to the commission for approval or denial at its next regularly scheduled meeting of the commission. No person shall sell or attempt to sell alcoholic beverages at wholesale or retail until they have received their city and state licenses authorizing them to do so. Applications for license shall be made on forms prescribed by the city clerk. 
(b)	Sworn statements. 
(1)	The applicant shall make a sworn statement of his qualifications according to this chapter and shall place such statement on file with the clerk before any license is issued; 
(2)	If the application covers a partnership, all members of the partnership must be qualified to obtain a license and must make sworn statements of those qualifications. 
(c)	In person. All applications for license shall be made in person. 
(d)	False information. Any statement on an application for license to sell alcoholic beverages which shall later be found to be false or which shall have omission of facts shall subject the applicant to prosecution for perjury under the laws of this state. 
(e)	Copy of state application. An applicant for a city license shall submit a copy of his state application at the time the local application is submitted to the city clerk. 
(f)	A consent statement by the applicant that all necessary investigation reports on the applicant and any employees in the applicant's establishment including, but not limited to, credit reports and reports from law enforcement agencies, may be obtained by the city. Any information in such reports may be furnished to the city clerk, and the applicant will be responsible for the cost thereof. If so requested, applicants shall also obtain such consent forms from each employee who will be employed in applicant's establishment. The applicant shall furnish the city a complete set of fingerprints. Such sets shall be forwarded to the state bureau of investigation. The city may require photographs of the applicant and/or fingerprinting and/or photographs of the applicant's employees for the purpose of conducting its investigation. 
(g)	The applicant. 
(1)	The applicant for the alcoholic beverage license shall be a citizen of the United States and the owner of the business; or if the owner of the business is a corporation, partnership or other legal entity, the applicant, who must be a citizen of the United States, must be a substantial and major partner or stockholder or the manager of the business responsible for the regular operation of said business on the premises for which the license is issued. The person who will have day-to-day operating responsibility for the business and who shall actively operate the business on a day-to-day basis, either the applicant or person designated by the applicant as the manager, shall reside within thirty (30) miles of the corporate limits of the city. 
(2)	The application shall include the name and address of the applicant; if a partnership, the names and residence addresses of the partners; if a corporation, names of the officers, the names and addresses of the registered agent for service of process, the name(s) of the manager(s), and the names of all shareholders holding more than twenty (20) percent of any class of corporate stock, or any other entity have a financial interest in each entity which is to own or operate the establishment for which a license is sought. If the manager changes, the applicant must furnish the city clerk the name and address of the new manager and other information as requested within three (3) days of such change. 
(3)	There shall be a fee of fifty dollars ($50.00) to defray investigative and administrative costs for the designation of a new manager on an existing license. 
(4)	All applicants shall furnish data, fingerprints, photographs, financial responsibility and other records as required by the city clerk to ensure compliance with the provisions of this chapter. Failure to furnish data pursuant to such request shall automatically serve to dismiss the application with prejudice. 
(5)	All licensed establishments must continuously maintain with the city the name and address of a registered agent upon whom any process, notice or demand required or permitted by law or under this chapter to be served upon the licensee or owner may be served. This person must be a resident of Pulaski County. The licensee shall file the name of such agent, along with the written consent of such agent, with the city clerk in such form as he or she may prescribe. 
(6)	In all instances in which an application is denied under the provisions of this chapter, the applicant may not reapply for a license for at least one (1) year from the final date of such denial. 
(7)	Each application for license under this chapter shall be accompanied by a separate check or cash in the amount of one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) to defray investigative and administrative costs. Any license application made pursuant to this chapter may be withdrawn by the applicant at any time. If the application is withdrawn before the license is issued, any sums deposited as license fees will be refunded. After issuance of the license, no refunds will be made. No refunds shall be made under any circumstances for investigative and administrative expenses required in this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 2012-3, § 3, 3-5-12)
Sec. 3-3. - General eligibility requirements. 
(a)	No alcoholic beverage license shall be granted to any person unless the person is twenty-one (21) years of age prior to filing an application for the license. 
(b)	When contrary to the public interest and welfare, no alcoholic beverage license shall be issued by the city to: 
(1)	Any person as determined by the city, by reason of such person's business experience, financial standing, trade associations, record of arrest, or reputation in any community in which he has resided, who is not likely to maintain the operation for which he is seeking a license in conformity with federal, state and local laws. 
(2)	Any person who has been convicted under any federal, state or local law of any felony involving moral turpitude. 
(3)	Any person who has been convicted under any federal, state or local law of any felony, not involving moral turpitude, within ten (10) years next preceding the filing of application for such license. 
(4)	Any person convicted under any federal, state, or local law of a misdemeanor, particularly, but not limited to, those involving retail liquor licenses, gambling, or tax law violations, if such conviction tends to indicate that the applicant will not maintain the operation for which he is seeking a license in conformity with federal, state or local laws. 
(c)	No retail license required by this division shall be granted to any person if such person retains for the operation of the license establishment an employee who has been convicted of a felony. 
(d)	No license for the sale of alcoholic beverages shall be granted to any person who has had any license issued under the law enforcement powers of the city previously revoked within two (2) years prior to the filing of the application. 
(e)	A license application may be denied to any applicant for any alcoholic beverage license where it appears that the application is intended to be a mere surrogate for a person or persons who would not otherwise qualify for a license for any reason whatsoever. 
(f)	No license for the sale of alcoholic beverages shall be granted to any person when the location for which the license is sought has had a license revoked within the last twelve (12) months. 
(Ord. No. 2012-3, § 3(2), 3-5-12)
Sec. 3-4. - Procedure for revocation and suspension of license; judicial review after denial or revocation. 
(a)	No license which has been issued or which may hereafter be issued by the city under this chapter shall be suspended or revoked, except for due cause as hereinafter provided. 
(b)	"Due cause" for the suspension or revocation of any license shall consist of any of the following: 
(1)	The failure of the licensee to comply with the terms, provisions, requirements and responsibilities of this chapter. 
(2)	The failure of the licensee to timely pay the annual license fee called for herein.
(3)	The violation by the licensee of any law regulating the sale of alcoholic beverages.
(4)	The conviction of the licensee of any felony, aggravated misdemeanor or drug related law. 
(5)	The licensee's permitting or maintaining a breach, or breaches, of the peace at licensee's establishment. 
(6)	The failure of the licensee or his employee to promptly report to the city and to the police department any violation of the laws or ordinances governing the licensing and sale of alcoholic beverages of which he has knowledge. 
(7)	The existence of any other condition which would make the continued operation of licensee's establishment detrimental, harmful or undesirable to the community. 
(c)	Upon information concerning any of the provisions outlined in this section herein above, the city shall serve notice upon licensee, personally or by mail addressed to licensee's establishment, requiring licensee to appear before the commission and show cause why the license should not be suspended or revoked. The hearing shall not be held sooner than three (3) days from the receipt of this notice, and the notice shall set forth the date, time and place of the hearing on the matter. This notice shall also state the condition alleged which could, if sustained, result in suspension or revocation of licensee's license. 
(d)	Within five (5) working days following the hearing on this matter, the commission shall render a decision, notifying licensee in writing of its decision by mail or by personally delivering it to licensee. In the event of revocation, no refund shall be made on any portion of any license fee paid, and the establishment will cease to operate upon notification. 
(e)	Following any decision denying an application for a license, or any decision for revoking or suspending an existing license, the applicant or licensee shall have the right to prompt judicial review in the manner provided by law. 
(Ord. No. 2012-5, § 1, 7-2-12)
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2012-5, § 1, adopted July 2, 2012, repealed § 3-4, in its entirety and enacted new provisions to read as herein set out. Prior to this amendment, § 3-4 pertained to similar subject matter. See Code Comparative Table for derivation. 
Sec. 3-5. - Posting of warning by retailer that consumption of alcohol during pregnancy is dangerous. 
(a)	All retail dealers and all retail consumption dealers who sell at retail, any alcoholic beverages for consumption on the premises shall post in a conspicuous place, a sign which clearly reads: "Warning: Drinking alcoholic beverages during pregnancy can cause birth defects." 
(b)	Any person who fails or refuses to post a sign as required in this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be fined in an amount not to exceed one hundred dollars ($100.00) for each violation. 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-2; Ord. of 11-22-06(1))
State Law reference- Posting of warning by retailer that consumption of alcohol during pregnancy is dangerous, O.C.G.A. § 3-1-5. 
Sec. 3-6. - Signs warning no drinking on premises, retailer/retail dealer of distilled spirits. 
    Every person engaged in the sale of distilled spirits, wine or malt beverages, other than licensees for consumption on the premises shall prominently display in such place of business a sign in bold letters: "Drinking of Alcoholic Beverages Prohibited on These Premises." 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-3; Ord. of 11-22-06(2))
Sec. 3-7. - Procedure for revocation and suspension of license. 
(a)	Any alcoholic beverage license which has been issued or which may hereafter be issued by the city may be suspended or revoked for due cause after a hearing held for the purpose of considering such suspension or revocation. At least three (3) days' prior written notice of time, place, and purpose of such hearing shall be given the holder of such license. The notice shall contain a statement of the charges upon which such hearing shall be held. 
(b)	Due cause for the suspension or revocation of any license shall consist of any of the following: 
(1)	The violation of any law, ordinance, or regulation made pursuant to lawful authority for the purpose of regulating such business. 
(2)	Change in circumstances of any licensee in such way that had such circumstances existed when the application was filed, the license would not have been granted. 
(3)	Any recurrent breaches of the peace, disturbances, or altercations occurring on licensed premises, or the failure of the licensee or his employee to promptly report to the city and the police department any violation of the laws or ordinances governing the licensing and sale of alcoholic beverages. 
(4)	The existence of any other condition which would make the continued operation of licensee's establishment detrimental, harmful, or undesirable to the community. 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-4)
Sec. 3-8. - Suspension in the event of disorder. 
    The city may suspend the sale of alcoholic beverages under any license issued in any emergency situation such as civil disorders or natural disasters or in any situation that the city deems such immediate suspension necessary for the protection of the health and welfare of the citizens of the city. Such suspension may be made effective immediately, and shall remain in force until the city determines the emergency is over or until the next meeting of the city council, at which time the suspension shall cease unless the suspension is extended by an affirmative action of the city council. 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-5)
Sec. 3-9. - Alcohol regulations relative to business hours. 
(a)	The provisions of this section shall be applicable to every licensee, agent, servant, and employee and any and all other persons affected. 
(b)	Except as otherwise provided herein, it shall be unlawful for any licensee or any other person to sell, offer for sale, or furnish to others any alcoholic beverages between the hours of 12:00 midnight and 8:00 a.m. on weekdays, and between the hours of 12:00 midnight on Saturday and 8:00 a.m. Monday. 
(c)	Licensees whose only sale of alcoholic beverages consist of beer and wine by the package may sell such beverages at any time except between 12:00 midnight on Saturday and 12:00 midnight on Sunday. 
(d)	No retail dealer or licensee for package sales of distilled spirits shall be in his or her place of business or open his or her place of business or furnish, sell, or offer for sale, any distilled spirits at any time prior to 8:00 a.m. or after 11:45 p.m. For purposes of this section, establishments will be considered open if, at any time past 11:45 p.m., there are persons inside the establishment other than regular employees who are engaged in activities to close, clean, or stock the establishment, or if the doors to the establishment are unlocked. The only exception to the above may be caused by emergency repairs to equipment and facilities. 
(e)	Licensees for the sale of malt beverages and/or wine for consumption on premises shall be and are subject to the following terms and conditions as to the sale of such beverages and hours of operation: 
(1)	Licensees for the sale of malt beverages and/or wine for consumption on premise shall not keep such establishments open between the hours of (12:00 a.m.) midnight and 6:00 a.m. on any day of the week; 
(2)	Said licensees shall not sell any alcoholic beverage between 12:00 midnight on Saturday and 6:00 a.m. on Monday; 
(3)	Licensees for the sale of malt beverages and/or wine for consumption on premises may be open from 6:00 a.m. on Sunday until 9:00 p.m. on Sunday but shall not at any time on Sunday sell, offer for sale, or furnish to others, any alcoholic beverages nor shall such licensee or any other person permit any person or entity to sell, offer for sale, furnish, or bring upon the premises any alcoholic beverage; 
(4)	No licensee for sale of malt beverage and/or wine for consumption on premises shall offer, provide or allow any live, recorded, or amplified musical performance or entertainment on the premises at any time on Sunday. 
(5)	Licensees shall be considered open if at anytime past midnight Monday through Saturday and past 9:00 p.m. on Sunday if there are persons inside the premises other than regular employees who are engaged in activities to close, clean, or stock the establishment, or if the doors to the establishment are unlocked. An exception to the above may be caused by emergency repairs to equipment and facilities. Consumption of alcoholic beverages on these premises is expressly prohibited at any time on Sunday. 
[(f)	Reserved.]
(g)	Licensees for the sale of distilled spirits for consumption on the premises shall not keep such establishments open between the hours of 12:00 o'clock a.m. (midnight) and 8:00 o'clock a.m. on any day of the week. The licensee shall not sell any alcoholic beverages after 11:45 o'clock p.m. on any day of the week. For purposes of this section, establishment will be considered open if at any time past 11:45 o'clock p.m. there are persons inside the establishment other than the regular employees who are engaged in activities to close, clean or stock the establishment or the doors to the establishment are unlocked. The only exception to the above may be caused by emergency repairs to equipment and facilities. The consumption of alcoholic beverages on these premises is expressly prohibited on Sundays. 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-6; Ord. of 1-3-97; Ord. of 7-16-97; Ord. of 10-15-97; Ord. of 10-4-00(2); Ord. No. 2006-4, 11-22-06) 
State Law reference- Days and hours of sale, O.C.G.A. §§ 3-3-7, 3-3-20. 
Sec. 3-10. - Sales of alcoholic beverages near churches, school buildings, or other sites. 
(a)	No person knowingly and intentionally may sell or offer to sell:
(1)	Any distilled spirits in or within one hundred (100) yards of any church building or within two hundred (200) yards of any school building, educational building, school grounds, or college campus; 
(2)	Any wine or malt beverages within one hundred (100) yards of any school building, school grounds, or college campus; 
(3)	Any distilled spirits, wine, or malt beverages within one hundred (100) yards of an alcoholic treatment center owned and operated by the state or by any county or municipal government. 
(b)	As used in this section the term "school building" or "educational building" shall apply only to state, county, school, or church school buildings and to such buildings at such other schools at which are taught subjects commonly taught in the common schools and colleges of this state. 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-7)
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2012-3, § 1, adopted Mar. 5, 2012, repealed § 3-10, in its entirety and renumbered § 3-7 as § 3-10. Former § 3-10, pertained to submission of license applcation; investigation. See Code Comparative Table for derivation. 
State Law reference- Sales near churches, schools, etc., O.C.G.A. § 3-21-1. 
Sec. 3-11. - Restroom facility entrance inside building only. 
    All toilets or restroom facilities maintained in the premises of any business engaged in the sale of alcoholic beverages shall be entered only from the inside of the building in which the business is conducted, and shall not be accessible from the outside. 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-8)
Sec. 3-12. - Oath required. 
    All applications for a license required to sell alcoholic beverages shall contain an oath providing that the information disclosed in the application is true and correct and providing further that each applicant will abide by, observe, and conduct the business according the provisions of this Code, ordinances of the city, the laws of the state and the rules and regulations of the state department of revenue in respect thereto. Each applicant shall sign the oath in the presence of the city clerk, or a notary public who shall witness the signing. 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-9)
Secs. 3-13-3-30. - Reserved.

Secs. 3-46-3-65. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - EXCISE TAX 

Sec. 3-66. - Imposed. 
(a)	Except as provided in subsection (b) of this section, there is hereby levied and imposed upon each wholesale dealer selling malt beverages within the city an excise tax in the amount of five cents ($0.05) per twelve (12) ounces and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of twelve (12) ounces of malt beverages sold by such wholesale dealer within the city. 
(b)	All malt beverages sold in or from a barrel or bulk container and being commonly known as tap or draft beer shall not be subject to the excise tax provided for in subsection (a) of this section. There is hereby imposed upon each wholesale dealer selling malt beverages within the city an excise tax of six dollars ($6.00) for each barrel or bulk container having a capacity of fifteen and one-half (151/2) gallons sold by such wholesale dealer within the city and at a like rate for fractional parts thereof. 
(c)	The excise taxes provided for in this section shall be in addition to any license fee, tax, or charge which may now or in the future be imposed upon the business of selling malt beverages at retail or wholesale, within the corporate limits of the city. 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-11)
State Law reference- Local excise tax required, O.C.G.A. § 3-5-80. 
Sec. 3-67. - Report; payment. 
(a)	Each wholesale dealer who has sold malt beverages within the city shall file a report by the tenth day of each month itemizing for the preceding calendar month the exact quantities, by size and type of container, of all malt beverages sold within the city for the month. Each such wholesale dealer shall remit to the city on the tenth day of the month next succeeding the calendar month in which such sales were made, the amount of excise tax due in accordance with this section. 
(b)	The failure to make a timely report and remittance shall render a wholesale dealer liable for a penalty equal to ten (10) percent of the total amount due during the first thirty-day period following the date such report and remittance were due and a further penalty of ten (10) percent of the amount of such remittance for each successive thirty-day period or any portion thereof during which such report and remittances are not filed. The filing of a false or fraudulent report shall render the wholesale dealer making such report liable for a penalty equal to twenty-five (25) percent of the amount of the remittance which would be required under an accurate and truthful report. Such failure to make a timely report or remittance, or the filing of a false or fraudulent report shall also constitute grounds for the revocation of the business license issued by the city to the wholesale dealer. 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-12)
State Law reference- Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 3-5-81. 
Secs. 3-68-3-80. - Reserved.

ARTICLE IV. - PACKAGE SALES OF DISTILLED SPIRITS[8] 
Footnotes: 
--- (8) --- 
State Law reference- Distilled spirits, O.C.G.A. § 3-4-1 et seq.

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 3-131. - Compliance with state and federal laws required. 
    In addition to all other rules and regulations, each application for a distilled spirits license and each distilled spirits licensee doing business in the city shall comply with all state and federal laws and the violation of any such laws and these regulations shall subject the licensee to the immediate revocation of his license and to criminal prosecution otherwise. 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-22)
Sec. 3-132. - Holder of retail dealers license authorized to sell only unbroken packages; breaking of package or packages or drinking of contents thereof on premises prohibited. 
(a)	All retailers and all retail dealers licensed under this article shall sell distilled spirits only in the original and unbroken package, which package shall contain not less than two hundred (200) milliliters. 
(b)	A person licensed under this article shall not permit the breaking of the package on the premises where sold and shall not permit the drinking of the contents of the package on the premises where sold. 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-23)
State Law reference- Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 3-4-25. 
Sec. 3-133. - Sale of other commodities prohibited; exceptions. 
(a)	No retailer licensed under this article shall sell or offer for sale or display or keep in stock at his place of business where distilled spirits are offered for sale, any other products or commodity except the following: 
(1)	Beer or wine, when properly licensed;
(2)	Beverages containing no alcohol which are commonly used to dilute distilled spirits;
(3)	Food for off-premises consumption;
(4)	Cigarettes and cigars.
(b)	No beverages of any kind may be opened or consumed in such place of business.
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-24)
Sec. 3-134. - Sales or deliveries outside retailer's place of business prohibited. 
    No retailer licensed under this article shall sell or deliver any distilled spirits to any person except in his place of business. 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-25)
Sec. 3-135. - Invoices. 
    Each person selling distilled spirits at retail for off-premises consumption, as a condition for license and doing business in the city, shall furnish to the city clerk a copy of all purchase invoices on or before the tenth of each month following such purchases. 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-26)
Sec. 3-136. - Storage of inventory. 
    A retailer or retail dealer licensed under this article shall keep no inventory or stock of distilled spirits at any place except his licensed place of business, and within his licensed place of business a storage place for distilled spirits shall be immediately adjacent to the room in which he is licensed to do business; there shall be but one (1) entrance to the storage space and this shall be through the retail store area. 
(Ord. of 7-23-91, § 3-27)
Secs. 3-137-3-150. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - RESERVED[9] 

Footnotes: 
--- (9) --- 
Editor's note-Ord. No. 2012-3, § 1, adopted Mar. 5, 2012, repealed Ch. 3, Art. IV, Div. 2, §§ 3-151-3-157, in its entirety. Former Div. 2, pertained to License. See Code Comparative Table for derivation.

Secs. 3-151-3-157. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - SALE OF DISTILLED SPIRITS BY THE DRINK 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 3-158. - Compliance with state and federal law required. 
(a)	In addition to all other rules and regulations, each applicant for a distilled spirits by the drink license and each distilled spirits by the drink licensee doing business in the city shall comply with all state and federal laws and the violation of any such laws and this ordinance and regulations promulgated pursuant to this article shall subject the licensee to immediate revocation of such license and to criminal prosecution as may be appropriate. 
(b)	In addition to all other rules and regulations, each applicant for a distilled spirits by the drink license and each distilled spirits by the drink licensees doing business in the city shall comply with all provisions of article I of chapter 3 of the Code of Ordinances and that such provisions shall apply to and are incorporated in this article. 
(Ord. No. 2006-5, 11-22-06)
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE 

Sec. 3-159. - Application for license; etc. 
(a)	License required. It shall be unlawful for any person to pour or offer to pour any distilled spirits within the corporate limits of the city without having a pouring license or to carry on such activity in violation of the terms of such license or this chapter. 
(b)	General qualifications. No license shall be granted to any person unless such person is a minimum of twenty-one (21) years of age and is a legal resident of the Oconee Judicial Circuit for a one-year period prior to filing an application for such license. 
(c)	License not transferable or assignable. No license for distilled spirits by the drink shall be transferable or assignable. 
(d)	No license shall be granted to any person for the operation of an establishment of selling distilled spirits for consumption on the premises of any area prohibited by law; nor shall any license be granted to any person for the operation of an establishment involving the sale of liquor by the drink in connection with the sale of drugs or pharmaceutical supplies. 
(e)	Annual license fee. The fee established in this article shall be in an amount determined by the board of commissioners. Such licenses shall run for a one-year period from the original date of issue and be renewed annually. 
(f)	Licenses granted under this article shall be prominently displayed in the licensee's establishment and shall be, together with the establishment, subject to inspection at any time by licensor or any law enforcement agency having jurisdiction in the area of licensee's establishment. 
(Ord. No. 2006-5, 11-22-06)
Sec. 3-160. - Gross revenue requirement. 
    No license for the sale of distilled spirits for consumption on the premises shall be granted to any person unless the licensee derives at least sixty (60) percent of his or her gross revenue from the sale of food and beverages other than alcoholic beverages. Applicant shall submit to the city clerk a certification by a certified public accountant that the applicant meets the requirements sent out herein. This certification shall be based upon a review of the applicant's total gross annual income for the license's location during the twelve (12) months immediately preceding the application for license under this section. If the applicant has been in business for less than twelve (12) months at the proposed location such certification shall be for the time that the applicant has been in business, annualized. An applicant filing an application for a new business will not be required to submit any certificates with the initial application, but instead the applicant must certify under oath that the person applying for the license intends to meet the requirements set out therein. A certification from a certified public accountant will be due monthly on the last calendar day of the month following the month for which the certification is made. 
(Ord. No. 2006-5, 11-22-06)
Sec. 3-161. - Fingerprinting of applicant. 
    The applicant for license to sell distilled spirits for consumption on the premises shall furnish a complete set of fingerprints. Such set shall be forwarded to the state bureau of investigation. 
(Ord. No. 2006-5, 11-22-06)
Sec. 3-162. - Brown bagging. 
    It shall be unlawful for a licensee under this article or any other commercial establishment to allow customers to bring with them their own alcoholic beverages, a practice which is commonly know as BYOB or brown bagging. 
(Ord. No. 2006-5, 11-22-06)
DIVISION 3. - EXCISE TAX 

Sec. 3-163. - Imposition of tax. 
    Tax is hereby imposed and levied upon the sale of spirits by the drink in the amount of three (3) percent of the charge to the public for such beverage. 
(Ord. No. 2006-5, 11-22-06)
DIVISION 4. - CERTAIN TYPES OF ENTERTAINMENT, ATTIRE AND CONDUCT PROHIBITED 

Sec. 3-164. - Certain types of entertainment, attire and conduct prohibited. 
    The following types of entertainment, attire and conduct are prohibited upon any premises licensed to sell, serve, or dispense alcoholic beverages for consumption on the premises; 
(1)	The employment or use of any person, in any capacity, in the sale or service of alcohol beverages while such person is unclothed or in such attire, costume or clothing, as to expose to view any portion of the female breast below the top of the areola or any portion of the male or female pubic hair, anus, cleft of the buttocks, vulva and genitals. 
(2)	Live entertainment where any person appears in the manner described in paragraph (1) of this section or where such person (or persons) perform(s) acts of or acts which simulate any of the following: 
a.	Sexual intercourse, masturbation, sodomy, bestiality, oral copulation, flagellation or any sexual act which is prohibited by law. 
b.	The caressing or fondling of the breasts, buttocks, anus or genitals.
c.	The displaying of the male or female pubic hair, anus, vulva or genitals.
(3)	The holding, promotion, sponsoring or allowance of any contest, promotion, special night, event or any other activity where patrons of the licensed establishment are encouraged or allowed to engage in any of the conduct described in paragraphs (1) and (2) above; provided, however, that nothing contained in this subsection (c) shall apply to the premises of any mainstream performance house, museum or theater which derives less than twenty (20) percent of its gross annual income from the sale of alcohol beverages. 
(Ord. No. 2006-5, 11-22-06)
Secs. 3-165-3-170. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - SPECIAL EVENT ALCOHOL BEVERAGE PERMIT 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 3-171. - Compliance with state and federal law required. 
    In addition to all other rules and regulations, each application for a special event alcohol beverage permit license and each special event alcohol beverage permit licensee doing business in the city shall comply with all state and federal laws and the violation of any such laws and these regulations shall subject the licensee to the immediate revocation of his license and to criminal prosecution otherwise. 
(Ord. No. 2012-1, § 2, 1-9-12)
Secs. 3-172-3-180. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LICENSE 

Sec. 3-181. - License required; commission approval; suspension of enforcing of certain law. 
    A special event alcohol beverage permit license is required for all special events that involve the sale and consumption of alcohol. Said license shall not be given without the prior approval of the commission. In the event said license is approved, the enforcement of section 11-9 shall be suspended in the area designated for the special event during the time of the special event. Provided, however, said suspension shall apply only to the drinking of alcoholic beverages sold by the licensee and only in the area designated for the special event. 
(Ord. No. 2012-6, § 1, 8-6-12)
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2012-6, § 1, adopted Aug. 6, 2012, repealed § 3-181, in its entirety and enacted new provisions to read as herein set out. Prior to this amendment, § 3-181 pertained to "License required." See Code Comparative Table for derivation. 
Sec. 3-182. - Period of license; business hours. 
(a)	A special event alcohol beverage permit license shall authorize the licensee to sell alcoholic beverages for consumption only on the premises for a period not to exceed three (3) days 
(b)	The special event alcoholic beverage permit shall be subject to all laws and ordinances regulating the time for selling such beverages including, but not limited to those outlined in section 3-6. 
(Ord. No. 2012-1, § 2, 1-9-12)
Sec. 3-183. - Place where permit valid; designation of area; patrons outside area; number of permits annually; adjacent property owners or renters of occupied parcels; notification of owners of property. 
(a)	The special event alcohol beverage permit shall be valid only for the place specified in the permit and the area where alcohol may be served shall be specifically delineated on the application. In no event shall patrons of the licensee go on to property not delineated on the application. Any suspension of the enforcement of any city ordinance contained herein shall not apply on property not delineated on the application. 
(b)	It shall be unlawful for licensees' employees or patrons of licensee to bring into or take outside the delineated area any alcoholic beverage or to furnish any alcoholic beverage to any person outside the delineated area. 
(c)	No more than six such permits may be issued to the applicant in any one calender year.
(d)	All applicants must provide proof that all adjacent property owners and/or renters of adjacent property have been notified of the application at least ten days prior to the event. 
(e)	The owner of the property where sales are to be made, if not the applicant, shall be notified in writing by the applicant of the application, and proof of said notification shall be attached to the application. 
(Ord. No. 2012-6, § 2, 8-6-12)
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2012-6, § 2, adopted Aug. 6, 2012, repealed § 3-183, in its entirety and enacted new provisions to read as herein set out. Prior to this amendment, § 3-183 pertained to "Place where permit valid; designation of area; patrons outside area; number of permits annually." See Code Comparative Table for derivation. 
Sec. 3-184. - License fee. 
    Each application for a special event alcoholic beverage permit shall be accompanied by a non-refundable fee in an amount as set by resolution of the commission, which amount shall remain in effect until modified or amended by subsequent resolution adopted by the city commission. 
(Ord. No. 2012-1, § 2, 1-9-12)
Sec. 3-185. - Application for license; time; review. 
(a)	Special event alcohol beverage permit license applications must be submitted at least forty-five (45) days prior to the planned special event. 
(b)	At least ten (10) days prior to the event, the applicant shall meet with the appropriate staff members of the City of Hawkinsville as designated by the city manager in order to review the application, area, conditions and restrictions pertaining to the event. Prior to the issuance of a permit for the event, the applicant shall sign a statement of understanding of and agreement to the terms and conditions imposed on the event. Such statements shall become a part of the conditions of the permit for the event. 
(Ord. No. 2012-1, § 2, 1-9-12)
Sec. 3-186. - Posting of license and notice; proof of license. 
(a)	All special event alcohol beverage permit licenses shall be posted at greeting areas or main entrances to the event. 
(b)	Every area where alcoholic beverages are consumed shall be conspicuously posted at all times at each point of entrance/exit with signs stating the following: "the possession of alcoholic beverages beyond this point is prohibited". The letters of such sign shall not be less than three (3) inches in height and one-half-inch (1/2") in width and shall be in black letters on a contrasting light background. 
(c)	City staff may ask event producers or business owners to show proof of license during the event. 
(d)	All employees working for the licensee during the event must be of legal age to drink.
(Ord. No. 2012-1, § 2, 1-9-12; Ord. No. 2012-6, § 3, 8-6-12)
Sec. 3-187. - Brown bagging. 
    It shall be unlawful for a licensee under this article or any other commercial establishment to allow customers or any of them to bring their own alcoholic beverages, a practice which is commonly known as BYOB or brown bagging. 
(Ord. No. 2012-1, § 2, 1-9-12)
Sec. 3-188. - General eligibility requirements. 
    All special event alcohol beverage permit licensee shall meet the general eligibility requirements outlined in section 3-153. 
(Ord. No. 2012-1, § 2, 1-9-12)
Sec. 3-189. - Revocation of license for failure to comply with state rules and regulations. 
    Licenses issued under this division shall be revocable in the event the licensee fails to comply with the rules and regulations of the state with the issuance of licenses for special event alcohol beverage permit and the state requirements pertaining to such issuance are hereby referred to and made a part hereof. 
(Ord. No. 2012-1, § 2, 1-9-12)
Sec. 3-190. - Security. 
    Licensees shall employ through the Pulaski County Sheriff's Office a minimum of two (2) officers for security at all times during the special event. 
(Ord. No. 2012-6, § 4, 8-6-12)
Sec. 3-191. - Patrons identification; containers of alcohol; cleaning up of site. 
(a)	Licensee must provide some type of acceptable identification tag for patrons and said identification tag shall be worn at all times while the patron is consuming alcohol during the special event. Persons consuming alcohol during the special event without such identification shall be subject to arrest in accordance with section 11-9. 
(b)	All alcohol sold must be in non-glass containers.
(c)	Licensee shall be responsible for all cleanup of the area designated for the sale and consumption of alcohol. 
(Ord. No. 2012-6, § 5, 8-6-12)
Chapter 4 - ANIMALS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note-An ordinance of July 1, 2002, amended ch. 4 in its entirety. Formerly, said chapter pertained to similar subject matter as adopted by the 1969 Code, as amended. See the Code Comparative Table.
Cross reference- Removal of animal carcasses, § 9-3; noise produced by dogs and cats, § 11-3(b)(3); animals and vehicles, § 15-2.
