Any person adversely affected by any determination made by the board relative to the issuance or denial of a certificate of appropriateness may appeal such determination to the board of commissioners. Any such appeal must be filed with the board of commissioners within fifteen (15) days after the issuance of the determination pursuant to subsection (f)(1) of this section or, in the case of failure of the board to act, within fifteen (15) days of expiration of the forty-five-day period allowed for board action. The board of commissioners may approve, modify, or reject the determination made by the board, if the governing body finds that the board abused its discretion in reaching its decision. Appeals from decisions of the board of commissioners may be taken to the superior court of the county in the manner provided by law for appeals from conviction for city ordinance violations. 
(j)	Variances. Where, by reason of unusual circumstances, the strict application of any provision of this article would result in the exceptional practical difficulty or undue hardship upon any owner of a specific property, the board, in passing upon applications, shall have the power to vary or modify provisions, so as to relieve such difficulty or hardship provided such variances, modifications, or interpretations shall remain in harmony with the general purpose and intent of the provisions, so that the architectural or historical integrity, or character of the property, shall be conserved and substantial justice done. In granting variances, the board may impose such reasonable and additional stipulations and conditions as will, in its judgement, best fulfill the purpose of this article. An undue hardship shall not be a situation of the person's own making. 
(k)	Recording of applications. The board shall keep a public record of all applications for certificates of appropriateness, and of all the board's proceedings in connection with the applications. 
(Ord. of 10-10-89, § V)
Sec. 5-102. - Same-Demolition or relocation. 
(a)	Authority to deny. The board shall have the authority to deny certificates of appropriateness of demolition or relocation of a historic property or district. 
(b)	Public hearing. A public hearing shall be scheduled for each application for a certificate of appropriateness for demolition or relocation. 
(c)	Consideration of post-demolition or post-relocation plans. The board shall not grant certificates of appropriateness for demolition or relocation without reviewing at the same time the post-demolition or post-relocation plans for the site. 
(d)	Criteria. Upon receipt of an application for a certificate of appropriateness for demolition or relocation, the board shall use the criteria described in section 5-101(g) to determine whether to deny the application or issue a certificate of appropriateness for demolition. 
(Ord. of 10-10-89, § VI)
Sec. 5-103. - Conformance to requirements. 
(a)	All work performed pursuant to an issued certificate of appropriateness shall conform to the requirements of such certificate. In the event work is not performed in accordance with such certificate, the board shall issue a cease and desist order and all work shall cease. 
(b)	The board of commissioners or the board shall be authorized to institute any appropriate action or proceeding in a court of competent jurisdiction to prevent any material change in the appearance of a designated historic property or historic district, except those changes made in compliance with the provision of this article or to prevent any illegal act or conduct with respect to such historic property or historic district. 
(Ord. of 10-10-89, § V(L))
Sec. 5-104. - Void if construction not commenced. 
    A certificate of appropriateness shall become void unless construction is commenced within six (6) months of the date of issuance. Certificates of appropriateness shall be issued for periods of eighteen (18) months and are renewable. 
(Ord. of 10-10-89, § V(M))
Sec. 5-105. - Maintenance of historic properties. 
(a)	Ordinary maintenance or repair. Ordinary maintenance or repair of any exterior architectural or environmental feature in or on a historic property to correct deterioration, decay or damage, or to sustain the existing form, that does not involve a material change in design, material or outer appearance thereof, does not require a certificate of appropriateness. 
(b)	Failure to provide ordinary maintenance or repair. Property owners of historic properties or properties within historic districts shall not allow their buildings to deteriorate by failing to provide ordinary maintenance or repair. The board shall be charged with the following responsibilities regarding deterioration by neglect: 
(1)	The board shall monitor the condition of historic properties and existing buildings in historic districts to determine if they are being allowed to deteriorate by neglect. Such conditions as broken windows, doors and openings which allow the elements and vermin to enter, the deterioration of exterior architectural features, or the deterioration of a building's structural system shall constitute failure to provide ordinary maintenance or repair. 
(2)	In the event the board determines a failure to provide ordinary maintenance or repair, the board will notify the owner of the property and set forth the steps which need to be taken to remedy the situation. The owner of such property will have thirty (30) days in which to do this. 
(3)	In the event that the condition is not remedied in thirty (30) days, the owner shall be punished as provided in section 5-44 and, at the direction of the board of commissioners, the board may perform such maintenance or repair as is necessary to prevent deterioration by neglect. The owner of the property shall be liable for the cost of such maintenance and repair performed by the board. 
(Ord. of 10-10-89, § VII(A), (B))
Chapter 6 - CEMETERIES[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Cemeteries and funerals, O.C.G.A. § 10-14-1 et seq.

Sec. 6-1. - Maintenance. 
    It shall be the duty of the city manager to see that the cemeteries are kept in proper condition. 
(Code 1969, § 6-2)
Sec. 6-2. - Disposition of revenue. 
    All revenue derived from the cemeteries of the city shall be paid into the treasury. 
(Code 1969, § 6-6)
State Law reference- Receipt of cemetery or burial lots in trust, annual returns, commissions, O.C.G.A. § 36-37-4; sale of municipal cemetery lots without acceptance of bids, O.C.G.A. § 36-37-6(b). 
Sec. 6-3. - Laying out and conveying lots. 
    Burial lots may be laid out at any time. The sizes of the lots shall be as determined by the board of commissioners, as shall the prices therefor. Title to the lot for interment only shall be made by the chairman of the board and the city clerk. Nonresidents of the city may buy lots. Lots of suitable size may be reserved for any public institution. A sufficient number of free lots shall be reserved for resident families who are unable to purchase. Ranges shall be laid out to bury strangers who may die in the city. The board of commissioners may donate lots to the poor, who shall improve them as required by the board of commissioners. No interment shall be permitted in any lot except free lots until the same is fully paid for and deed made to the deceased person's family. 
(Code 1969, § 6-9)
Sec. 6-4. - Reversion of lots. 
    Free cemetery lots improved by those to whom they are donated by the board of commissioners upon condition of such improvements shall revert to the city upon removal of the owner from the city or the extinction of the family without occupying the lot. Any lot sold or donated and the terms not complied with shall revert to the city. Should the owner of any unoccupied lot remove from the city and not transfer his right to someone else before the expiration of three (3) years, at the expiration of such time it shall revert to the city. All future deeds must contain this provision. 
(Code 1969, § 6-11)
Sec. 6-5. - Depth of graves; superintendence of burial. 
    All bodies shall be interred in a grave not less than three and one-half (31/2) feet deep or in a properly constructed vault and in no case shall they be permitted to remain aboveground enclosed with brick or other materials. No corpse shall be interred except under the superintendence or direction of the city manager. 
(Code 1969, § 6-12)
Chapter 7 - CIVIL DEFENSE[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Fire protection and prevention, Ch. 8; police, Ch. 12; traffic, Ch. 17.
State Law reference- Georgia Mutual Aid Act, O.C.G.A. § 36-69-2 et seq.; Georgia Emergency Management Act of 1981, O.C.G.A. § 38-3-1 et seq.; Interstate Civil Defense and Disaster Compact, O.C.G.A. § 38-3-70.

Sec. 7-1. - Civil defense. 
    As used in this chapter the term "civil defense" shall include measures necessary to provide for the mobilization, organization and direction of the civilian populace and necessary support agencies to prevent or minimize the effects of fire, flood, storm, earthquake and epidemic as well as the effects of enemy or subversive activities against the populace, communities, industrial plants, facilities and other installations. 
(Ord. of 6-29-83, § I)
Sec. 7-2. - Council of civil defense-Membership. 
    The Hawkinsville-Pulaski County council of civil defense is hereby created and shall include the following: 
(1)	City manager;
(2)	Director of civil defense (as appointed);
(3)	Police chief;
(4)	Fire chief;
(5)	City health officer;
(6)	City engineer;
(7)	County or city welfare officer;
(8)	American Red Cross representative;
(9)	Others, including representatives of business, labor and patriotic organizations, as appointed by the council. 
(Ord. of 6-29-83, § II)
Sec. 7-3. - Same-Powers and duties. 
    It shall be the duty of the Hawkinsville-Pulaski County council of civil defense and it is hereby empowered to: 
(1)	Develop a city civil defense plan. This plan shall provide for the effective mobilization of all the resources of the city, both private and public. 
(2)	Prepare and recommend for consideration by the board of commissioners ordinances necessary to implement the civil defense plan. 
(3)	Consider and recommend to the board of commissioners for approval mutual aid plans and agreements. 
(4)	Have other powers and duties as determined locally.
(Ord. of 6-29-83, § III)
Sec. 7-4. - Civil defense director. 
    There is hereby created the office of the Hawkinsville-Pulaski County civil defense director. Such officer shall be nominated by the chairman and appointed by the governor as provided by law. The civil defense director is hereby charged to: 
(1)	Represent the chairman on all matters pertaining to civil defense;
(2)	Obtain and utilize cooperation of city and county officials in the preparation and implementation of civil defense plans; 
(3)	During periods of emergency, direct the services of all city civil defense forces;
(4)	During periods of emergency, obtain vital supplies and equipment lacking, needed for the protection of life and property of people and bind the city for the value thereof and, if required immediately, requisition same. 
(Ord. of 6-29-83, § IV)
Sec. 7-5. - Civil defense corps-Generally. 
    Officers and employees of the city with volunteer forces enrolled to aid them during an emergency and all groups, organizations and persons who make the agreements on operation of law are charged with duties necessary for the protection of the life and property in the city and during such an emergency shall constitute the civil defense corps. 
(Ord. of 6-29-83, § V)
Sec. 7-6. - Same-Divisions. 
    The functions and duties of the Hawkinsville-Pulaski County civil defense corps shall be distributed among the divisions as listed below. Each division shall be under the direction of an assistant deputy director appointed by the council of civil defense. The assistant deputies will be selected from among the best qualified in the city and may include but not be restricted to chiefs of existing community services. Arranged within each division are the various civil defense services, each service under the direction of a chief designated to head this service due to his intimate knowledge of the particular service and his qualities as a leader. The divisions are as follows: 
(1)	Communications and warning;
(2)	Public information;
(3)	Search, rescue and recovery;
(4)	Police services;
(5)	Evacuation;
(6)	Fire control;
(7)	Engineering;
(8)	Transportation services;
(9)	Petroleum and solid fuels;
(10)	Utilities;
(11)	Hazardous materials control;
(12)	Health, medical and social services;
(13)	Radiological defense;
(14)	Administrative services;
(15)	State military support;
(16)	Coordination of private organizations and volunteers;
(17)	Training (optional);
(18)	Shelter and temporary housing;
(19)	Damage assessment and reporting;
(20)	Public property assistance;
(21)	Nuclear attack civil protection.
(Ord. of 6-29-83, § VI)
Sec. 7-7. - Volunteers. 
    All persons other than officers and employees of the city volunteering in service pursuant to the purposes of this chapter shall serve with or without compensation. While engaged in such service, they shall have the same immunities as persons and employees of the city performing similar duties. 
(Ord. of 6-29-83, § VII)
Sec. 7-8. - Violations during emergency. 
    It shall be a misdemeanor punishable by fine not to exceed five hundred dollars ($500.00) and by imprisonment not to exceed six (6) months, or both, for any person during an emergency to: 
(1)	Willfully obstruct, hinder or delay any member of the civil defense corps in any enforcement of a lawful rule or regulation issued pursuant to this chapter or in the performance of any duty imposed upon him by virtue of this chapter; 
(2)	Do any act forbidden by any lawful rules or regulations issued pursuant to this chapter if such act is of such a nature as to give assistance to the enemy; 
(3)	Wear or carry or display without authority any mark or identification specified by the council of civil defense. 
(Ord. of 6-29-83, § VIII)
Sec. 7-9. - Civil defense plan. 
    A complete and adequate civil defense plan shall be formulated by the council of civil defense and chiefs of divisions. This plan will be based upon plans formulated in the state, mutual aid agreements. 
(Ord. of 6-29-83, § IX)
Chapter 8 - FIRE PROTECTION AND PREVENTION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Buildings and building regulations, Ch. 5; fireworks, § 11-5; police, Ch. 12; streets and sidewalks, Ch. 15; traffic, Ch. 17.
State Law reference- Authority to provide police and fire protection, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a); The Uniform Act for the Application of Building and Fire Related Codes to Existing Buildings, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-200; providing of fire escapes by building owners, O.C.G.A. § 8-2-50; obstruction or hindering of firefighters, O.C.G.A. § 16-10-24.1; regulation of fire and other hazards to persons and property generally, O.C.G.A. § 25-2-1 et seq.; local fire departments generally, O.C.G.A. § 25-3-1 et seq.; firefighter standards and training, O.C.G.A. § 25-4-1 et seq.; mutual aid resource pacts, O.C.G.A. § 25-6-1; regulation of fireworks, O.C.G.A. § 25-10-1 et seq.

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 8-1. - Adoption of fire prevention code. 
(a)	For the purpose of prescribing regulations governing conditions hazardous to life and property from fire, explosion, or exposure to hazardous materials, the city adopts the 1987 edition of NFPA 1, Fire Prevention Code of the National Fire Protection Association, together with its incorporated standards and codes as listed in Annex A of such code and together with appendices A, B, E, H, I and K, save and except such portions as are deleted in the sections that follow. 
(b)	Such code and appended material are hereby incorporated by reference and referred to throughout this article as the NFPA Fire Prevention Code. 
Sec. 8-2. - Annual appropriation for fire department. 
    For the support and maintenance of the fire department, the board of commissioners shall annually make a proper appropriation in its discretion for the fire department. 
(Code 1969, § 8-1)
Sec. 8-3. - Personnel; care of equipment. 
    The fire chief shall have authority to appoint assistants and employees subject to approval of the city manager. The fire chief shall have the care and management of its respective hoses, ladders, hooks and apparatus for extinguishing fires. 
(Code 1969, § 8-2)
Sec. 8-4. - Authority of fire chief or acting chief at fires. 
    The chief of the fire department shall have supreme and absolute control and command of the fire department at all fires, and in his absence the assistant chief shall be vested with his authority, and in the absence of both the above-named officers, the same authority shall devolve through the proper chain of command as designated by the fire chief. 
(Code 1969, § 8-3)
Sec. 8-5. - Obstructing fire station or appurtenances. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully put any trash or other obstructions in front of any fire house, or other appurtenance of or belonging to the fire department. 
(Code 1969, § 8-4)
Sec. 8-6. - Persons allowed at fire scene. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person, except firefighters, the city manager, members of the police force, owners or agents of the property endangered by fire, and interested insurance company representatives, to be within the immediate limits of operation during the progress of any fire in the city, unless ordered there by the officers in command of the fire department or officers of the city. 
(Code 1969, § 8-5)
State Law reference- Obstruction or hindering of firefighters, O.C.G.A. § 16-10-24.1. 
Sec. 8-7. - Injuring fire apparatus. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully or intentionally drive over, injure or damage in any way or by any means whatever, any engine, hose, hook, ladder or other implement, material or apparatus belonging to, connected with or used by any fire company in the city as a part of its machinery for extinguishing fires. 
(Code 1969, § 8-6)
State Law reference- Crossing fire hose, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-248. 
Secs. 8-8-8-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - HAZARDOUS DWELLINGS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference- Authority for municipalities to repair, close or demolish unfit buildings or structures, O.C.G.A. § 41-2-7 et seq.

Sec. 8-26. - Authority to condemn. 
    Any dwelling house perilous to life or property by reason of its rundown condition, lack of repair, its contents or other hazardous conditions, likely to cause the spreading of fire or impede the combatting of fire, may be condemned. 
(Ord. of 11-9-76, § 1)
Sec. 8-27. - Examination of dwelling; notice to owner to correct defects. 
    Whenever the board of commissioners has information that there is within the city any dwelling house which is a fire hazard, it shall cause an examination to be made. If after such report or inspection by the board it is determined that the building is a hazard, the board shall serve notice on the owner and the person in possession directing him to repair, make safe or demolish the building and thereby eliminate such hazard. 
(Ord. of 11-9-76, § 2)
Sec. 8-28. - Failure to comply with notice; issuance of summons. 
    Upon the failure of the owner or person in possession to obey the notice served pursuant to section 8-27, the board of commissioners shall cause a summons to be served on the owner or person in possession requiring him to show cause at a time and place designated in such notice, but not less than ten (10) days from the date of service thereof, why the dwelling should not be condemned. 
(Ord. of 11-9-76, § 3)
Sec. 8-29. - Hearing; presentation of evidence. 
    At a hearing under this article the city and the owner may present evidence to the board of commissioners concerning the condition of the building and the complaint of the city that same constitutes a fire hazard. After consideration of the evidence, the city may permit the owner to take steps to repair or make safe the building or it may adjudge that it be condemned. 
(Ord. of 11-9-76, § 4)
Sec. 8-30. - Demolition order. 
    If after the hearing under this article the board of commissioners determines that the dwelling cannot be repaired or put in a safe condition, it may render a judgment that the dwelling be demolished by the owner within a specified number of days, but not less than sixty (60) days from the date of judgment, and that upon the owner's failure to demolish it, the city may accomplish the demolition at the expense of the owner. 
(Ord. of 11-9-76, § 5)
Sec. 8-31. - Factors of consideration; standards. 
    In passing on the question of condemning a dwelling, the board of commissioners shall be guided by these standards as to the condition of the dwelling: 
(1)	Whether the dwelling is occupied or vacant;
(2)	The general state of repair;
(3)	The materials from which the building was constructed and its fire potential;
(4)	Deteriorated or inadequate foundations;
(5)	Defective or deteriorated flooring or floor supports;
(6)	Members of walls, partitions or other vertical supports that are of insufficient size or condition to carry loads with safety; 
(7)	Ceilings, roof supports and roofs that may be inadequate to hold the weight they were designed or placed to hold; 
(8)	Fireplaces or chimneys which list, bulge or settle due to defective materials or deterioration, or are of insufficient size or strength to carry imposed loads with safety; 
(9)	Members of ceilings, roof or walls, or other members in the building which sag, split or buckle due to defective material or deterioration; 
(10)	Deteriorated or defective exterior walls, roof, foundations, floors, broken windows, doors, deteriorated and crumbling plaster; 
(11)	Broken, rotted, split or buckled exterior wall coverings or roof coverings;
(12)	Any part or portion of the dwelling which is in a condition to cause a fire or explosion or provide a ready fuel to augment the spread and intensity of fire or explosion arising from any cause. 
(Ord. of 11-9-76, § 6)
Sec. 8-32. - Justification of condemnation. 
    Before condemning a dwelling, the board of commissioners must find that the same violates the standards set forth in section 8-31 and its judgment shall specify the conditions which justify its condemnation. 
(Ord. of 11-9-76, § 7)
Sec. 8-33. - Posting of notices, orders. 
    All notices and decisions under this article shall be posted on the dwelling itself in a conspicuous place thereon in addition to the service of notice required to the owner. If the owner resides outside of the city, notice may be served by certified mail at his last known address. 
(Ord. of 11-9-76, § 8)
Sec. 8-34. - Demolition by city-Recovery of costs. 
    If it shall be necessary after condemnation for the city to demolish the dwelling at its expense, costs for such demolition shall be recorded and charged to the owner. Should the owner fail to pay the costs promptly, the city clerk shall issue execution in favor of the city, which shall issue and be levied as executions for taxes in the city are issued and levied. Such executions may be recorded in the office of the clerk of the superior court of the county and constitute a lien against the property. 
(Ord. of 11-9-76, § 9)
Sec. 8-35. - Same-Notice of intent to owner, occupant. 
    Should the city demolish the hazardous structure, it shall give the owner and the person in possession at least fifteen (15) days' notice of its intention to do so before actual destruction begins. 
(Ord. of 11-9-76, § 10)
Sec. 8-36. - Penalty. 
    If any owner fails to comply with any decision of the board of commissioners under this article after proper notice, he is subject to punishment as for violation of the ordinances of this city. 
(Ord. of 11-9-76, § 11)
Chapter 9 - HEALTH AND SANITATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Hazardous dwellings, § 8-26 et seq.; obstructing drainageways, § 11-12; solid waste management, Ch. 14; utilities, Ch. 18.

ARTICLE I. - LITTER CONTROL[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note-Ord. No. 2013-5, adopted Nov. 4, 2013, deleted Art. I, §§ 9-1-9-5, in its entirety and enacted new provisions to read as herein set out. Prior to this amendment, Art. I pertained to "In General." See Code Comparative Table for derivation.

Sec. 9-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Commercial handbill means a printed or written matter, any sample or device, circular, leaflet, pamphlet, paper, booklet, or any other reproduced originals or copies of any matter of literature that: 
(1)	Advertises for sale any merchandise, product, commodity, or thing; or
(2)	Directs attention to any business or mercantile or commercial establishment, or other activity, for the purpose of either directly or indirectly promoting the interest thereof by sales; or advertises any meeting, theatrical performance, exhibition, or event of any kind, for which an admission fee is charged for the purpose of private gain or profit. 
    Garbage means decaying animal and vegetable wastes resulting from the handling, preparation, cooking and consumption of food. 
    Litter means "garbage," "refuse," and "rubbish" and other waste material which, if thrown or deposited, tends to create a danger to public health, safety and welfare. 
    Noncommercial handbill means any printed or written matter, any sample, or device, circular, leaflet, pamphlet, newspaper, magazine, paper, or booklet not included in the definition of a "commercial handbill." 
    Private premises means any dwelling, house, building, or other structure, designed or used either wholly or in part for private residential purposes and shall include any yard, grounds, walk, driveway, porch, steps, vestibule or mailbox appurtenant to such dwelling, house, building, or other structure. 
    Public place means any and all streets, sidewalks, boulevards, alleys or other public ways and any and all public parks, squares, spaces, grounds and buildings. 
    Refuse means all decomposing and decaying solid wastes (except body wastes), including garbage, rubbish, ashes, street cleanings, dead animals, and industrial wastes. 
    Rubbish means nondecaying solid wastes consisting of both combustible and noncombustible wastes, such as paper wrappings, cigarettes, cardboard, tin cans, yard clippings, leaves, wood, glass, bedding, crockery and similar materials. 
(Ord. No. 2013-5, 11-4-13)
Sec. 9-2. - Litter in public places. 
(a)	Generally. No person shall throw or deposit litter in or upon any street, sidewalk or other public place within the city except in public receptacles or in authorized private receptacles for collection. 
(b)	Placement of litter in receptacles so as to prevent scattering. Persons placing litter in public receptacles or in authorized private receptacles shall do so in such a manner as to prevent it from being carried or deposited by the elements upon any street, sidewalk or other public place or upon private property. 
(c)	Sweeping litter into gutters prohibited. No person shall sweep into or deposit in any gutter, street or other public place within the city the accumulation of litter from any building or lot or from any public or private sidewalk or driveway. Persons owning or occupying property or a business establishment shall keep the sidewalk and curb area in front of their premises free of litter; however, nothing contained in this section shall prohibit the temporary deposit of litter designated for pick-up by the city public works department. 
(Ord. No. 2013-5, 11-4-13)
Sec. 9-3. - Vehicle litter. 
(a)	Litter thrown by persons in vehicles. No person, while a driver or passenger in a vehicle, shall throw or deposit litter upon any street or other public place within the city, or upon private property. 
(b)	Truck loads causing litter. No person shall drive or move any truck or other vehicle within the city unless such vehicle is so constructed or loaded as to prevent any load, contents or litter from being blown or deposited upon any street, alley or other public place. 
(Ord. No. 2013-5, 11-4-13)
Sec. 9-4. - Litter in parks, bodies of water. 
(a)	Litter in parks. No person shall throw or deposit litter in any park within the city except in public receptacles and in such a manner that the litter will be prevented from being carried by the elements upon any part of the park or upon any street or other public place. Where public receptacles are not provided, all such litter shall be carried away from the park by the person responsible for its presence and properly disposed of elsewhere. 
(b)	Litter in lakes and fountains. No person shall throw or deposit litter in any fountain, pond, river, stream, creek or any other body of water in a park or elsewhere within the city. 
(Ord. No. 2013-5, 11-4-13)
Sec. 9-5. - Handbills. 
(a)	Throwing or distributing commercial handbills in public places. No person shall throw or deposit any commercial handbill in or upon any sidewalk, street or other public place within the city, nor shall any person hand out or distribute or sell any commercial handbill in any public place. Provided, however, that it shall not be unlawful on any sidewalk, street, or other public place within the city for any person to hand out or distribute, without charge to the receiver thereof, any noncommercial handbill to any person willing to accept it. 
(b)	Placing commercial and noncommercial handbills on vehicles. No person shall throw or deposit any commercial or noncommercial handbill in or upon any vehicle except directly to any driver or passenger willing to accept it. 
(c)	Distributing commercial and noncommercial handbills at inhabited private premises. No person shall throw, deposit or distribute any commercial or noncommercial handbill in or upon private premises, except by handing or transmitting any such handbill directly to the owner, occupant, or other person then present in or upon such private premises. The provisions of this subsection shall not apply to the distribution of mail, nor to newspapers, nor to the delivery of packages or freight. 
(Ord. No. 2013-5, 11-4-13)
Sec. 9-6. - Property owner's responsibility; abatement by city; costs constitute lien. 
(a)	Owner to maintain premises free of litter. The owner or person in control of any private property shall at all times maintain the premises free of litter. Provided however, that this section shall not prohibit the storage of litter in authorized private receptacles for collection. 
(b)	Rubbish, overgrown bushes and weeds, and machinery prohibited. It shall be unlawful for the owner, renter or lessee of any real property or the holder of any easement on any real property within the city to allow such property to be dumping place for rubbish of all kinds and descriptions, become overgrown with bushes and weeds twelve (12) inches in height, or become unsightly with junk machinery, either of which is considered a nuisance and is punishable. 
(c)	Clearing of litter, rubbish, overgrown bushes and weeds and machinery from private property by city. 
(1)	The city through its officers, is authorized and empowered to notify the owner of any private property within the city, or the agent of such owner, to properly dispose of litter located on such property, or to order the clearing of overgrown bushes and weeds and junk machinery, which is dangerous to public health, safety and welfare. 
(2)	Upon the failure, neglect, refusal of any owner or agent so notified, to comply with the terms of this section within ten (10) days after receipt of written notice, or such notice's return due to inability to make registered delivery, the city is hereby authorized and empowered to pay for disposing of such litter or the removal of overgrown bushes and weeds and junk machinery. 
(3)	When the city has effected the clearing of such property or has paid for such clearing to be accomplished so that the private property complies with this section, the actual cost thereof, plus an administrative fee of one hundred dollars ($100.00), plus accrued interest at the rate of twelve (12) percent per annum from the date of the completion of the work, if not paid by the owner, shall be charged to the owner of such property on the next regular tax bill. 
(4)	When the full amount due the city is not paid within thirty (30) days, there shall be recorded in the property records of the county courthouse, a sworn statement showing the cost and expense incurred for the work, the date the work was done, and the legal description of the property. The recordation of such sworn statement shall constitute a lien on the property, and shall remain in full force and effect for the amount due in principal and interest, plus cost of court, reasonable attorney fees for collection, until final payment has been made. Sworn statements recorded shall be prima facie evidence that all legal requirements have been complied with and that the work has been done properly and shall be full notice to every person concerned that the amount of the statement, plus interests and costs, constitutes a charge against the property designated or described in the statement and that the same is due and collectible as provided by law. 
(d)	If the owner or person in control of said private property has, within the previous six (6) months, been given notice of a violation of this section, the city officials and employees shall be authorized to immediately issue a citation for a subsequent violation without the requirement of additional notice or opportunity to cure. 
(e)	Nothing in this section shall preclude the city from enforcing the terms of this section by way of immediate issuance of a citation for any violation thereof. 
(Ord. No. 2013-5, 11-4-13)
Sec. 9-7. - Penalties. 
    A violation of this article shall subject the violator to the maximum punishment provided section 1-12 of this Code. A separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day during which a violation occurs or continues. 
(Ord. No. 2013-5, 11-4-13)
Secs. 9-8-9-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - WELLS[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Water Well Standards Act of 1985, O.C.G.A. § 12-5-120; abandoned wells or holes, abatement of hazard, O.C.G.A. § 44-1-14.

Sec. 9-26. - Permit required. 
    It shall be unlawful and a violation of the laws and ordinances of this city for any person to dig or cause to be dug any well within the corporate limits of the city until a written application for a permit for such well has been passed on and approved by the board of commissioners. 
(Ord. of 10-21-75)
Sec. 9-27. - Permit application. 
(a)	Any person desiring to dig or cause to be dug a well within the corporate limits of the city shall first apply in writing to the board of commissioners of such proposal to dig a well and set forth in such application information concerning the location of the proposed well, anticipated depth of the proposed well and the uses to be made of the same. The application shall set forth the name of the person who shall dig or bore the well with the proposed method to be used in digging. Details, including the size and depth of such boring, shall be specified in the application. 
(b)	The application filed with the city clerk shall be signed by the person on whose property the well is to be dug and by the person or representative of the firm which proposes to bore or dig the well, affirming those statements made in the application to be true. 
(Ord. of 10-21-75)
Sec. 9-28. - Hearing. 
    Upon the filing of an application for a permit under this article, the applicant shall be notified of the time and place of a hearing to be held by the board of commissioners on the application as to whether or not permission will be granted for such digging. The applicant may appear before the board of commissioners on the question of whether the permit should be granted and present evidence and argument in his own behalf. 
(Ord. of 10-21-75)
Sec. 9-29. - Recording, notice of board action on applications. 
    The board of commissioners shall consider the application for a permit under this article and all the facts and circumstances and either grant the permit or deny the application for the permit. In either event, the action of the board of commissioners shall be recorded and the city clerk shall notify the applicant of the action taken by the board on the application. 
(Ord. of 10-21-75)
Sec. 9-30. - General guideline principles. 
    The board of commissioners, in passing upon applications for permits to dig wells, repair the same, install pumps or abandon wells, shall be guided by the standards as set forth herein. In passing on such applications, the board shall be guided by the duty to protect the health and sanitation of the citizens of the city and should take into account that hazards usually increase where the water table is at a comparatively shallow depth, particularly in populous areas. Sewer lines, septic tanks, leaching fields, fertilizers, industrial wastes, pesticides and other chemicals, cesspools, outdoor toilets and other like conditions are potential sources of contaminants and pollutants. Improperly constructed wells and abandoned wells can be avenues for carrying contaminants to the aquifer. If the top of the well is not properly protected, surface contaminants can enter the well and the groundwater. Similarly, if the space between the wall of the drill holes and the casing is not sealed in the upper part of the well and if this space is not protected from pollution down to the water table, then the space surrounding the casing can act as a conduit for carrying pollutants to the aquifer. These general principles shall be standards or guidelines in applying the more particular standards as set forth herein and in passing on whether or not permission shall be granted or denied on any application referred to herein. 
(Ord. of 10-21-75)
Sec. 9-31. - Factors of consideration generally. 
(a)	The board of commissioners shall grant or deny the well permit after considering:
(1)	The location of the proposed well and its effect on the water supply in the immediate area of the proposed well and underground waters nearby, as well as the general supply of water lying underground in and about the city. 
(2)	The general porosity of the soil in the area in which the well is proposed to be dug, taking into account the septic tanks in the general vicinity which will affect the water supply in and about the area where the well is proposed to be bored. Drain lines from such septic tanks as may be in the area and other factors affecting the surface water and seepage shall be considered in this respect. 
(3)	The proposed method of construction as outlined by the applicant shall be considered, taking into account protective measures proposed to be used to prevent pollution of underground waters and any underground source of waters which the proposed well may tap. 
(4)	Any other factor which may bear upon the water supply of the city and the sources of the supply, including the density of population in and about the area in which permission is sought to dig the well. 
(b)	The board shall not arbitrarily deny a permit for the digging of a well. In all applications an opportunity shall be given for hearing before the board of commissioners by the applicant in support of his application. 
(Ord. of 10-21-75)
Sec. 9-32. - Determining factors, standards. 
    The board of commissioners shall grant or deny the permit under this article after considering the factors hereinafter set forth which shall be determining factors or standards in granting or denying the permit: 
(1)	The geological formations and structures underlying the area in which the well is proposed to be dug must be suitable for the purpose; 
(2)	Hydrology and hydraulic characteristics of the aquifers;
(3)	Density of population;
(4)	Estimated demands for water;
(5)	Depth to the groundwater table;
(6)	Character of subsoil formation;
(7)	Quality of groundwater;
(8)	Depletion rate of groundwater resources;
(9)	Sources of groundwater pollution;
(10)	Such other factors as may be relevant to the protection of the public health.
(Ord. of 10-21-75)
Sec. 9-33. - Requirements provided for in application. 
    The application for a permit under this article shall contain such pertinent information as may be required by the board of commissioners in passing on the application and the application shall require the applicant to provide information in the drilling of the well as follows: 
(1)	Construction and drilling information:
a.	Log of formations encountered;
b.	Depth of finished well;
c.	Diameter of drilled hole;
d.	The depth of formation stabilizer (gravel pack);
e.	Size of particles if used;
f.	Depth and thickness of grout;
g.	Casing information: length, inside diameter, well thickness, type of material;
h.	Screen information: length, trade name, inside and outside diameter, slot size, type of material; 
i.	Static water level;
j.	Water level when pumped at the designed rate;
k.	Yield of well in gallons per minute or hour.
(2)	Requirements for drilling:
a.	The city shall be assured that the well will be constructed and dug in an area which can be kept in a sanitary condition. 
b.	It shall be constructed in such a manner as to maintain insofar as practicable existing natural protection against pollution of water-bearing formations and to exclude pollutants from known sources. 
c.	The construction of the well should seal off, insofar as practicable, water-bearing formations that are or may be polluted. 
d.	The well shall be constructed so that no unsealed opening will be left around the well. 
e.	The city shall be assured that the well is located so that it is protected from surface waters and from seepage from sources of contamination and pollution. 
f.	The city shall be assured by the owner and the well driller that the well casing shall extend at least twelve (12) inches above the final grade of the land surface. The earth surrounding the casing shall slope away from the well and shall be firmly tapped to prevent water from seeping down around the casing. The space between the casing and the well of the drill hole shall be filled with cement grout to a depth of at least ten (10) feet. The minimum thickness of the cement or grout shall be four (4) inches. The space between the casing and the wall of the drill hole in the remaining distance to the static water level should be filled with grout. 
(Ord. of 10-21-75)
Sec. 9-34. - Repair of wells. 
    No well shall be repaired, altered or modified in any way without first obtaining permission from the board of commissioners. To effect repairs to an existing well, application must be made setting forth pertinent information as to the name of the owner of the property where the well to be repaired is located, the person who is to perform the repairs and a description of the repairs to be made, together with a statement of the manner in which the well is to be resealed and disinfected. Such application shall be submitted in the same manner as an application to dig a well as set forth herein, and the applicant shall have notice and opportunity to be heard as to whether permission will be granted for such repairs to be made. In passing on such an application for repairs, the standards to guide the board in granting or denying such permit are: 
(1)	The proposed method of repairs as outlined by the applicant shall be taken into consideration, including but not limited to the protective measures proposed to be used to prevent pollution of underground waters and any underground source of water which this well taps, together with any other factor which may bear upon the water supply of the city and the sources of such supply. 
(2)	In any repairs or alterations to an existing well, the same shall be disinfected with a chlorine solution. 
(3)	After repairs, a water sample must be collected and analyzed for bacterial acceptance.
(Ord. of 10-21-75)
Sec. 9-35. - Pump installations. 
    Before any pump is installed, either in a new well or in the repairs of an existing well, the top of the well must be completed in a way that will insure the protection of the groundwaters from surface contamination. This completion includes providing proper drainage away from the well, sealing the space between the walls and the drill hole and the well casing and closing the space between the pump, pipe and the casing. Installing a new pump shall be considered as a repair and all the rules governing repairs or alterations of a well shall apply should a pump be installed for any purpose. 
(Ord. of 10-21-75)
Sec. 9-36. - Abandonment of wells. 
    Wells which will no longer be used as a water supply shall be plugged to prevent entrance of surface water, filth or any other substances which might pollute or contaminate the groundwater. The casing may be withdrawn and the well filled with chlorinated sand to a distance of five (5) feet above the static water level. The balance of the distance to the ground surface shall be filled with clean earth, firmly tapped. If the casing is not removed, it shall be cut away below the ground surface and the filling procedure as set forth herein shall be carried out. Any test holes that may be dug shall be plugged in a manner that does not allow the entrance of surface water or any other material that might pollute or contaminate the groundwater. Plugging procedures may vary to suit the geological condition at the test hole site. 
(Ord. of 10-21-75)
Sec. 9-37. - Disposal wells. 
    Under no circumstances shall a well of any type be drilled, dug or excavated, nor shall any existing well be used for the purpose of receiving sewage, liquid or solid waste, rubbish, garbage or any other waste material. 
(Ord. of 10-21-75)
Sec. 9-38. - Connection to present city water mains prohibited. 
    No person given permission to dig a well shall be permitted to attach to or remain attached to any existing city water main or line held or operated by the city. Under no conditions may any private well permitted under the procedures as outlined in this article be connected or joined with the public water supply of the city. 
(Ord. of 10-21-75)
Sec. 9-39. - Report to city after completion of well. 
(a)	The board of commissioners may grant or deny the permit to dig a well based on the considerations as outlined in this article. In either event, the applicant shall be notified of the action taken by the board on his application. 
(b)	If his application is granted, such applicant shall conform to all the rules and standards set forth by the board and upon completion of the well shall report to the city clerk that the well has been dug and is complete and ready for use. The city shall make an inspection to determine that its rules and regulations have been complied with in all respects. An analysis shall be made of the water from such well and this analysis report passed on with the compliance provisions of such permit. Before any use of the well is permitted and any water drawn therefrom for consumption or domestic use, the applicant shall obtain a certificate of compliance and final permit from the city clerk for use of such well. 
(Ord. of 10-21-75)
Sec. 9-40. - Violation. 
    Any person who willfully violates the provisions of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and punished under the provisions applicable to violation of city ordinances. The use of a well in violation of this article shall be considered as a continuing violation so that each day any violation continues shall be considered as a separate violation and punishable as such. 
(Ord. of 10-21-75)
Secs. 9-41-9-50. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - WELLHEAD PROTECTION 

Sec. 9-51. - Short title and purpose. 
(a)	This article shall be known as the "Wellhead Protection Ordinance."
(b)	The purpose of this article is to insure the provision of a safe and sanitary drinking water supply for the city by the establishment of wellhead protection zones surrounding the wellheads for all wells which are the supply sources for the city water system and by the designation and regulation of property uses and conditions which may be maintained within such zones. 
(Ord. of 7-5-00, § 1)
Sec. 9-52. - Definitions. 
    When used in this article the following words and phrases shall have the meanings given in this section: 
    Hazardous waste or material means any waste or material which because of its quantity, concentration or physical, chemical or infectious characteristics may: 
(1)	Cause or significantly contribute to an increase in mortality or an increase in serious irreversible or incapacitation reversible illness; or 
(2)	Pose a substantial present or potential hazard to human health or to the environment when improperly treated, stored, transported, disposed of or otherwise managed. 
    Sanitary landfill means a disposal site where solid wastes, including putrescible waste or hazardous waste, are disposed of on land by placing earth cover thereon. 
    Wellhead means the upper terminal of a well, including adapters, ports, seals, valves and other attachments. 
(Ord. of 7-5-00, § 2)
Sec. 9-53. - Establishment of wellhead protection zone. 
    There is hereby established a use district to be known as a wellhead protection zone, identified and described as all the area within a circle the center of which is the center of any city water supply wellhead and the radius of which is one hundred fifty (150) feet. 
(Ord. of 7-5-00, § 3)
Sec. 9-54. - Permitted uses. 
    The following uses shall be permitted within wellhead protection zones; 
(1)	Any use permitted within existing agricultural or single family residential districts, except that the minimum residential lot size for a lot any portion of which lies within the wellhead protection zone shall not be less than one acre; and 
(2)	Any other open land use where any building located on the property is incidental and accessory to the primary open land use. 
(Ord. of 7-5-00, § 4)
Sec. 9-55. - Prohibited uses. 
    The following uses or conditions shall be and are hereby prohibited within the wellhead protection zones, whether or not such use or condition may otherwise be ordinarily included as a part of a use permitted under section 9-54 of this article. 
(1)	Surface use or storage of hazardous material, expressly including commercial use of agricultural pesticides; 
(2)	Septic tanks or drain fields appurtenant thereto;
(3)	Impervious surfaces other than roofs of buildings and streets, driveways and walks serving buildings permitted under section 9-54 of this article; 
(4)	Sanitary landfills;
(5)	Hazardous waste disposal sites;
(6)	Stormwater infiltration basins;
(7)	Underground storage tanks;
(8)	Sanitary sewer lines within one hundred fifty (150) feet of a wellhead.
(Ord. of 7-5-00, § 5)
Sec. 9-56. - Administration. 
    The policies and procedures for administration of any wellhead protection zone established under this article, including without limitation those applicable to non-conforming uses, exceptions, enforcement and penalties, shall be the same as provided in the existing zoning ordinance for the City of Hawkinsville, as the same is presently enacted or may from time to time be amended. 
(Ord. of 7-5-00, § 6)
Secs. 9-57-9-60. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - INOPERATIVE MOTOR VEHICLES 

Sec. 9-61. - Definitions. 
    Inoperative motor vehicle means any motor vehicle, which is to include automobiles, cars, trucks, motorcycles, recreational vehicles, 4-wheelers, campers, and any other vehicle which may be driven upon public or private lands, which has been discarded, dismantled, wrecked, scrapped, ruined or junked and is not in operating condition including all parts and accessories for said inoperative motor vehicle; or which for a period of thirty (30) days or longer, has been partially or totally disassembled by the removal of tires, wheels, engine or other essential part required for the operation of the vehicle. 
    Property means any public or private property in the City of Hawkinsville, except for property on which is located a licensed business for the sale, restoration, maintenance, painting or repair of the above-described motor vehicles. 
(Ord. of 7-7-08)
Sec. 9-62. - Storage of inoperative motor vehicles. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to keep, except within a fully enclosed building or structure or otherwise shielded or screened from public view, on any property unless properly zoned or permitted, any motor vehicle, trailer, or semitrailer, which is inoperative or which has no current license plate or tag. 
(Ord. of 7-7-08)
Sec. 9-63. - Notice to owner. 
    If it is determined that any inoperative motor vehicle as defined above exists on any property within the City of Hawkinsville, the code enforcement officer, city manager, or designee of the city manager, or any law enforcement officer shall notify in writing the owner, the tenant, the owner's agent, or the property manager or person in possession of the property that conditions in violation of this article exist and must be abated within thirty (30) days. 
(Ord. of 7-7-08)
Sec. 9-64. - Removal by city. 
    If any person fails to remove from his or her property such inoperative motor vehicle after receiving notice required in section 9-63 above, the city, through its employees or agents may remove any such inoperative motor vehicle, and the cost of any such removal and disposal shall be chargeable to the owner of the vehicle or premises and may be collected by the city as taxes and levies are collected. 
(Ord. of 7-7-08)
Sec. 9-65. - Penalties. 
    A violation of any section in this article shall subject the violator to the maximum punishment provided under section 4.13 of the City Charter. A separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day during which a violation occurs or continues. 
(Ord. of 7-7-08)

Chapter 11 - OFFENSES[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Obstructing fire station or appurtenances, § 8-5; persons allowed at fire scene, § 8-6; injuring fire apparatus, § 8-7; unclean lots, § 9-1; littering, § 9-2; weeds, § 9-4; wells, § 9-26 et seq.; municipal court, Ch. 10; police, Ch. 12; solid waste management, Ch. 14; streets and sidewalks, Ch. 15; traffic, § 17; utilities, Ch. 18.
State Law reference- Limitations on home rule powers of municipal corporations, O.C.G.A. § 36-35-6(a)(2); criminal code of Georgia, O.C.G.A. § 16-1-1 et seq.

Sec. 11-1. - Driving on municipally owned racetrack. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person to drive a motor vehicle upon the race tracks of the city commonly and generally used by horses in training. No person shall drive his motor vehicle upon the track surface between the rails thereof and that area kept and maintained for use by horses in training on any of the various municipally owned race tracks of the city. 
(b)	The board of commissioners shall have the power and authority to grant a permit for any purpose reasonably necessary so that one might cross over or pass around municipally owned race tracks in a motor vehicle for purposes reasonably necessary in maintenance and upkeep or for some other purpose deemed to be necessary or useful and not harmful to the track itself. 
(c)	A motor vehicle, for the purpose of this section, shall be defined in the same manner and in the same way as motor vehicles are defined in the Georgia Law of Motor Vehicles. 
(d)	Any person who violates this section shall be punished as for a misdemeanor under the charter of this city. 
(Ord. of 2-10-76)
Sec. 11-2. - Driving while under influence of alcohol or drugs. 
    It is unlawful and punishable by confinement in the city jail and/or a fine not exceeding the state limit for any person to: 
(1)	Drive any vehicle on the streets and roads of this city while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, beer, wine or other beverages; 
(2)	Drive any vehicle on the streets and roads of this city while under the influence of any narcotic drug, or under the influence of any other drug to a degree which renders him incapable of safely driving a vehicle. 
(Code 1969, § 17-17)
Cross reference- Alcoholic beverages, Ch. 3; traffic, Ch. 17. 
State Law reference- Driving under the influence of alcohol or drugs, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-391. 
Sec. 11-3. - Noise. 
(a)	The creation of any unreasonably loud, disturbing and unnecessary noise within the limits of the city is prohibited. Noise of such character, intensity or duration as to be detrimental to the life or health of any individual, or in disturbance of the public peace and welfare is prohibited. In addition, at any time between 9:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. Sunday through Thursday and 11:00 p.m. Friday night and Saturday night and 9:00 a.m. Saturday and Sunday, it shall be deemed a violation of this section if any noise regulated or prohibited under the provisions of this section is readily audible in another home, residence, apartment or building in which the usual openings such as windows and doors are closed. The person causing the noise, or the owner, lessee or other person in control of the property from which the noise is emanating, shall be deemed to be in violation of this section. 
(b)	The following acts, among others, are declared to be loud, disturbing and unnecessary noises and noises in violation of this section, but this enumeration shall not be deemed to be exclusive, namely: 
(1)	Horns. The sounding of any horn or signal device on any automobile, motorcycle, bus or other vehicle while not in motion except as a danger signal if another vehicle is approaching apparently out of control or, if in motion, only as a danger signal; the creation by means of any such signal device of any unreasonably loud or harsh sound or the sounding of such device for an unnecessary or unreasonable period of time. 
(2)	Radios, phonographs, musical instruments. The playing of any radio, phonograph or any musical instrument in such a manner or with such volume as to annoy or disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of persons in any office, hospital or in any dwelling, hotel or other type of residence, or any persons in the vicinity, except this section shall not apply to schools of music between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 10:00 p.m. 
(3)	Voices. Yelling, shouting, hooting, whistling or singing at any time or place so as to annoy or disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of persons in any hospital, dwelling, hotel or other type of residence, or any persons in the vicinity. The provisions of this section shall also apply to voices or other noise originating within a building or residence and to noise produced by animals such as dogs, cats or others, whether housed in a building or an open enclosure, and if the noise continues steadily or intermittently during a period in excess of ten (10) minutes in any one day or night. In the case of animals, the owner or person in immediate control of the property on which the animal is housed shall be deemed responsible. In the case of noise emanating from a residence or apartment, the owner, lessee, renter or other person deemed to be in immediate control of the home, apartment or building shall be deemed to be responsible. It shall be deemed a violation of this section if the noise caused by persons or animals is readily audible in any nearby home, apartment, building or other structure when its natural openings such as doors and windows are closed. 
(4)	Vehicles. The use of any automobile, motorcycle or vehicle so out of repair, so loaded or in such manner as to create loud and unnecessary grating, grinding or rattling or other noise. 
(5)	Steam whistles. The blowing of any steam whistle attached to any stationary boiler, except to give notice of the time to begin or stop work, or as a warning of fire or danger, or upon request of proper city authority. 
(6)	Exhausts. To discharge into the open air the exhaust of any stationary steam engine, stationary internal combustion engine, motor vehicle or motorboat engine, except through a muffler or other device which will effectively prevent loud or explosive noises therefrom. 
(7)	Construction work. The erection (including excavation), demolition, alteration or repair of any building in any residential district or section, the excavation of streets and highways in any residential district or section, other than between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 10:00 p.m., except in the cases of urgent necessity and then only with a permit from the code enforcement officer, which permit may be granted for a period not to exceed sixty (60) days while the emergency continues. If the code enforcement officer determines that the public health and safety will not be impaired by the erection, demolition, alteration or repair of any building or the excavation of streets and highways within the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m., and if he further determines that loss or inconvenience would result to any party in interest, the code enforcement officer may grant permission for such work to be done within the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m., upon application being made at the time the permit for work is awarded or during the progress of the work. 
(8)	On streets adjacent to school, hospital, etc. The creation of any excessive noise on any street adjacent to any school, institution of learning, church or court while the same are in session, or adjacent to any hospital, which unreasonably interferes with the workings or sessions thereof. 
(9)	Loudspeakers on vehicles. The use of mechanical loudspeakers or amplifiers on trucks or other moving or standing vehicles for advertising or other purposes if such use is readily audible pursuant to subsection (a) above. 
(c)	None of the foregoing terms or prohibitions shall apply to or be enforced against:
(1)	Any vehicle of the city while engaged upon necessary public business;
(2)	Excavations or repairs of bridges, streets or highways, by or on behalf of the city, county, state, during the night season, when the public welfare and convenience renders it impossible to perform such work during the day; nor shall the same apply to work performed by public utility companies under like conditions and circumstances, or when there is urgent necessity therefor; 
(3)	The reasonable use of amplifiers or loudspeakers in the course of public addresses which are noncommercial in character. 
(d)	The prohibitions shall not be applicable to any parade, celebration or performance for which a written permit has been obtained prior thereto from the city manager. 
(e)	It shall be unlawful to use, maintain or operate loudspeakers, sound trucks, amplifiers or other mechanical or electrical devices or audio or radio systems in or outside of motor vehicles which can readily be heard from a reasonable distance or as set forth in subsection (a), for increasing the volume of sound, upon the streets, sidewalks, parks or other public places of the city; provided, that nothing in this section shall apply to the United States, the state, the county or the city, nor to public agencies. 
(f)	Penalty. A violation of this section or any subpart thereof shall be punishable by a fine of two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) for the first offense and by a fine of four hundred ($400.00) for any subsequent offense thereof. 
(Ord. of 7-12-88; Ord. of 9-17-97)
Sec. 11-4. - Parades, demonstrations, public addresses. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to participate in any parade, demonstration or public address on the streets of the city, unless written consent therefor has been granted by the city manager. 
(Code 1969, § 11-3)
Cross reference- Streets and sidewalks, Ch. 15. 
Sec. 11-5. - Fireworks. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to set off, light, explode, or shoot any firecracker, explosive, Roman candle, sparkler, or pyrotechnic of any type whatsoever, within the city. 
(Code 1969, § 11-7)
Cross reference- Fire protection and prevention, Ch. 8. 
State Law reference- Regulation of fireworks, O.C.G.A. § 25-10-1 et seq. 
Sec. 11-6. - Shooting of firearms. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to shoot firearms in the city, except persons legally enforcing the law. 
(Code 1969, § 11-8)
State Law reference- Discharge of firearms, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-103 et seq. 
Sec. 11-7. - Ball playing in streets. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to play ball by throwing, tossing or catching the same for amusement or pastime, or otherwise, on the streets of the city. 
(Code 1969, § 11-9)
Sec. 11-8. - Bill posting. 
    It shall be unlawful for anyone to put any bill or placard upon any wall, fence, building, post or other property of another without permission of the owner. It shall be unlawful for any person to put any bill or placard on any telephone pole or electric light pole in the city. 
(Code 1969, § 11-10)
State Law reference- Prohibited placements of campaign posters, signs and advertisements, O.C.G.A. § 21-1-1; unlawful placement of signs within right-of-way of public road, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-51. 
Sec. 11-9. - Drinking in public. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to drink spirituous or malt or intoxicating liquors upon any street or alley or upon any sidewalk within the city. 
(Code 1969, § 11-11)
Cross reference- Alcoholic beverages, Ch. 3. 
State Law reference- Public drunkenness, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-41. 
Sec. 11-10. - Cutting, injuring trees, flowers, etc. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to cut, break, destroy, mutilate or otherwise injure or damage any of the trees, plants, shrubbery, flowers or other public ornament or public convenience on the streets, sidewalks or alleys of the city, or in any public parks or in any of the public school grounds or in the cemeteries. 
(Code 1969, § 11-12)
Sec. 11-11. - Abandoned refrigerators, other containers accessible to children. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to leave in a place accessible to children any abandoned, unattended or discarded icebox, refrigerator or any other container of any kind which has an airtight door or lock which may not be released for opening from the inside of such icebox, refrigerator or container. Any person guilty of violating the same shall, except in cases of manifest justification, be punished as prescribed in section 1-12. 
(Ord. of 11-10-87(2), § 11-13)
State Law reference- Abandonment of containers which lock or fasten automatically, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-100. 
Sec. 11-12. - Obstructing drainageways. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to throw any trash or other thing whatever or obstruct in any way whatever any ditch, gutter or drain, or in any way impede or prevent the free flow of water through such drain, ditch or gutter. 
(Code 1969, § 10-3)
Cross reference- Solid waste management, Ch. 14; utilities, Ch. 18. 
Sec. 11-13. - Conduct in auditorium. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in any conduct in the city auditorium which would disrupt or disturb any show or entertainment therein, or which would result in the destruction of property therein, or which would create an unhealthful situation therein, or which would disturb or annoy the other occupants of the auditorium. 
(Code 1969, § 12-7)
Sec. 11-14. - Midnight curfew. 
(a)	It is unlawful for any minor seventeen (17) years of age or younger to loiter, wander, stroll or play in or upon or be upon public streets, sidewalks, highways, roads, alleys, parks, playgrounds or other public grounds, public places, public buildings, places of amusement, eating places, vacant lots or any place unsupervised by an adult over the age of eighteen (18) years having lawful parental authority over such minor or an adult who is the lawful guardian of such minor, between the hours of 12:00 o'clock midnight on any day and 5:00 o'clock a.m. of the following day; and provided that the provisions of this section shall not apply in the following instances: 
(1)	When a minor is accompanied by his or her parent, guardian or other adult person having the lawful care and custody of the minor; 
(2)	When the minor is upon an emergency errand directed by his or her parent or guardian or other adult person having the lawful care and custody of such minor; 
(3)	When the minor is returning directly home from a school activity or entertainment, and school sponsored or school related events, including recreational activities or dances; 
(4)	When the minor is returning directly home from lawful employment that makes it necessary to be in the above referenced places during the prescribed period of time; 
(5)	When the minor is attending or traveling directly to or from an activity involving the exercise of First Amendment rights of speech, freedom of assembly or free exercise of religion; 
(6)	When the minor is in a motor vehicle with parental consent or the consent of the lawful guardian for normal travel with interstate travel through the city excepted in all cases from the curfew; 
(7)	When the minor is on the property of the building in which he or she resides.
    Any acts made unlawful by the provisions of this section shall be subject to and shall subject the violator to the juvenile code and all laws respecting juveniles of this state. The report shall be made and forwarded to the appropriate juvenile authority for prosecution as may be appropriate. 
(b)	Responsibility of parents. It shall be unlawful for the parent, guardian or other person having custody or control of any child seventeen (17) years of age or younger to permit or by insufficient control to allow such child to be in or upon public streets or any other places listed in subsection (a) above within the city between the hours of 12:00 o'clock midnight on any day and 5:00 o'clock a.m. of the following day except in circumstances set forth in subsections (1) through (7) of subsection (a). Upon conviction of this section for the first time, a person shall be given a warning by the court. Such warning shall be entered on the court records for filing. Upon further convictions, a person shall be subject to such punishment as the municipal court of the city may impose, subject to all limitations contained in the Charter of the city. Each violation of this section shall constitute a separate offense. 
(c)	This section shall be effective on July 31, 1995 at noon.
(Ord. of 7-31-95)
Sec. 11-15. - Littering. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person or persons to place, throw, dump, leave, deposit or cause to be permitted any litter on any public or private property within the municipal limits of this city unless: (1) the property is designated by the city or its agencies for the disposal and persons authorized by the proper public authority to use such property; (2) the litter is placed into a litter receptacle or container installed on such property; or (3) the person is the owner or tenant in lawful possession of such property or has first obtained the consent of the owner or tenant in lawful possession or unless the act is done with the personal direction of the owner or tenant, all in a manner consistent with the public welfare. 
(b)	As used in this section the term:
    "Litter" means all discarded sand, gravel, slag, brickbats, rubbish, waste material, tin cans, refuse, garbage, trash, debris, dead animals, bottles, boxes, containers, tobacco products, tires, appliances, mechanical equipment or parts, building or construction materials, tools, machinery, wood, and all other discarded material or substance of every kind and description resulting from domestic, industrial, commercial or other operation. 
    "Public or private property" means the right-of-way of any road or highway; any body of water or watercourse and the shores or beaches thereof; any park, playground, building, refuge, or conservation or recreation area, and residential or farm properties, timberlands, or forests. 
(c)	Whenever litter is thrown, deposited, dropped, dumped or otherwise removed from any motor vehicle, boat, airplane, or other conveyance in violation of this section it shall be prima-facia evidence that the operator of the conveyance has violated this part. 
(1)	Except as is hereinabove provided whenever any litter which is dumped, deposited, thrown or otherwise left on public or private property in violation of this section is discovered to contain any article or articles including but not limited to letters, bills, publications or other writings which display the name of the person thereon in such a manner as to indicate that the article belongs or belonged to such person, it shall be a rebuttable presumption that such person has violated this section. 
(d)	Any person who violates this section shall upon conviction thereof be punished as follows: 
(1)	By a fine of two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) for the first offense and by a fine of four hundred dollars ($400.00) for a subsequent offense thereof. 
(Ord. of 9-17-97)
Editor's note- An Ordinance of Sept. 17, 1997, enacted provisions to establish a new section 11-14. Said section had been previously established by an Ordinance of July 31, 1995, hence, inclusion as § 11-15 was at the editor's discretion. 
State Law reference- Littering, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-40 et seq. 
Sec. 11-16. - Activities prohibited after midnight 
(a)	Definitions. 
(1)	Premises shall mean any property owned, leased or otherwise occupied or in the possession or control of any person, firm, corporation or other entity and shall embrace the entire building and also all of the land on which the building stands as well as any vacant land whereupon any activity may be conducted. 
(2)	Entertainment activity shall mean the presentation, appearance, participation in or enjoyment of any musical, theatrical, educational or other event whether live, recorded, or partially live and partially recorded. 
(b)	It shall be unlawful for any person, firm, corporation or other legal entity to cause, permit or allow between the hours of 12:00 midnight and 7:00 a.m. the following: 
(1)	Entertainment activity wherein any fee, cover charge, admission or other remuneration of any kind is charged. 
(2)	Any act or activity prohibited in section 11-3 of this chapter of the code. 
(Ord. No. 2012-4, § 1, 5-7-12)
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2012-4, § 1, adopted May 7, 2012, repealed § 11-16, in its entirety and enacted new provisions to read as herein set out. Prior to this amendment, § 11-16 pertained to similar subject matter. See Code Comparative Table for derivation. 
Sec. 11-17. - Driving or parking upon Veteran's Memorial Park also known as "River Front Park". 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to drive any motorized vehicle across, over, through or permit the operation of such motor vehicle, or park or otherwise allow any motor vehicle to remain upon Veteran's Memorial Park also known as "River Front Park" at any time after 6:00 p.m. on any day of the week. Any person guilty of violating this section shall be punished as provided in section 1-12 of the Code of Ordinances of the City of Hawkinsville, Georgia. 
(Ord. of 10-4-00(3))
Editor's note- An Ordinance of Oct. 4, 2000, enacted provisions to establish a new section 11-16. Inasmuch as section 11-16 was previously established by an Ordinance of Oct. 15, 1997, inclusion as § 11-17 was at the editor's discretion. 
Sec. 11-18. - Public nudity. 
(a)	As used in this section:
(1)	"Nude" means the showing of: 
a.	Human male or female genitals or pubic area with less than a fully opaque covering; or 
b.	Any portion of the anal cleft or cleavage of the male or female buttocks. Attire that is insufficient to comply with this requirement includes, but is not limited to, G-strings, T-backs, thongs, and any other clothing or covering that does not completely and opaquely cover the anal cleft or cleavage of the male or female buttocks; or 
c.	The portion of the human female breast directly or laterally below a point immediately above the top of the areola with less than a fully opaque covering; this definition shall include the entire lower portion of the human female breast, but shall not include any portion of the cleavage of the human female breast exhibited by a dress, blouse, shirt, leotard, bathing suit, or other clothing, provided the areola is not exposed; or 
d.	Human male genitals in a discernibly turgid state, even if completely and opaquely covered. 
(2)	"Person" means any live human being aged ten (10) years of age or older. 
(3)	"Place provided or set apart for nudity" means enclosed single sex public restrooms, enclosed single sex functional shower, locker and/or dressing room facilities, enclosed motel rooms and hotel rooms designed and intended for sleeping accommodations, doctor's offices, portions of hospitals, and similar places in which nudity or exposure is necessarily and customarily expected outside of the home and sphere of privacy constitutionally protected therein. This term shall not be deemed to include places where a person's conduct of being nude is used for his or her profit or where being nude is used for the promotion of business or is otherwise commercially exploited. 
(4)	"Public place" means any location frequented by the public, or where the public is present or likely to be present, or where a person may reasonably be expected to be observed by members of the public. Public Places include, but are not limited to, streets, sidewalks, parks, beaches, business and commercial establishments (whether for profit or not for profit, whether open to the public at large, or whether entrance is limited by a cover charge or membership requirement), hotels, motels, restaurants, night clubs, country clubs, cabarets, and meeting facilities utilized by any religious, social, fraternal or similar organization. Premises, or portions thereof, such as hotel rooms, used solely as a private residence, whether permanent or temporary in nature, shall not be deemed to be a public place. 
(b)	It shall be unlawful for any person to knowingly or intentionally appear nude in a public place or in any other place that is readily visible to the public, except a place provided or set apart for nudity. It shall also be unlawful for any person or entity maintaining, owning, or operating any public place to operate and to knowingly, or with reason to know, permit or allow any person to appear nude in such public place, except a place provided or set apart for nudity. 
(c)	A person violating subsection (3) of this section is guilty of a misdemeanor and, on conviction, shall be punished by a fine not exceeding five hundred dollars ($500.00) or be imprisoned not exceeding six (6) months, or both. 
(d)	This section shall not be deemed to address photographs, movies, video presentations, or any other non-live performances. 
(e)	This Act may be prosecuted by a city or county attorney or by private action brought by an aggrieved party in a court of competent jurisdiction. 
(Ord. of 3-3-03)
Sec. 11-19. - Indecent exposure.
