(3)	A business or practitioner which has locations in Georgia subject to occupation tax by more than one local government in Georgia shall only be subject to occupation tax by the City of Hawkinsville for the number of employees who are employed within the corporate limits of the City. This limitation shall only apply when the business or practitioner has provided to the city satisfactory proof of current payment of the occupation tax of the other local government(s). 
(4)	If an employee works for the same business or practitioner in more than one municipal corporation or county and the business or practitioner submits proof of this, the employee shall be counted as an employee in the city only if the city is the jurisdiction where such employee works for the longest period of time within the calendar year. 
(d)	If a business or practitioner commences business in the city on or after January 1 in any year, the occupation tax for the remaining portion of the year shall be fifty (50) percent of the tax imposed for the entire year. The administrative fee shall not be reduced. 
(e)	If a business or practitioner does not know how many employees, which are the basis of this occupation tax, will be employed by the business or practitioner during the current calendar year, then the business or practitioner shall file a return estimating the number of employees, which are the basis of this occupation tax. If such estimate is not accurate, then no later than June 30 the business or practitioner shall file an amended return indicating the actual number of employees during the previous calendar year. Any overpayment of the occupation tax may be credited to the business or practitioner's account for future tax liability, offset against other amounts due and owing to the city for any reason or paid to the business or practitioner at the discretion of the city clerk. 
(f)	Real estate brokers shall be subject to occupation tax pursuant to this ordinance only if they maintain a principal or branch office in the city. 
(Ord. of 2-6-95)
Sec. 16-76.5. - Occupation tax certificate. 
    Every business, practitioner and location subject to payment of the occupation tax levied by this article shall display a current occupation tax certificate in a conspicuous place at the location for which such certificate was issued. If the taxpayer does not have a permanent location within the city, the occupation tax certificate shall be shown to any police officer or the city clerk upon request. 
(Ord. of 2-6-95)
Sec. 16-76.6. - Practitioners of professions and occupations. 
    Practitioners of professions and occupations as defined in this article shall pay the occupation tax as set forth in section 16-76.4 above or shall pay an occupation tax of four hundred dollars ($400.00) per practitioner. On the tax return for 1995 or such later time as the practitioner first commences business in the city, the practitioner shall elect a method of taxation. Such election shall be changed for subsequent calendar years only by a written request filed by the practitioner on or before February 1 of the year in which the election is to be changed. 
(Ord. of 2-6-95)
Sec. 16-76.7. - Exemptions. 
(a)	No occupation tax shall be levied on the following:
(1)	Any practitioner whose office is maintained by and who is employed in practice exclusively by the United States, the state, a municipality or county of the state, or instrumentality of the United States, the state, or a municipality or county of the state; 
(2)	Those businesses regulated by the Georgia Public Service Commission;
(3)	Those electrical service businesses organized under Chapter 3 of Title 46 of the Official Code of Georgia; 
(4)	Any farm operation for the production from or on the land of agricultural products, but not including any agribusiness; 
(5)	Non-profit, agricultural product cooperative marketing associations pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 2-10-105; 
(6)	Motor common carriers pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 46-7-15;
(7)	Persons purchasing guano, meats, meal, flour, bran, cottonseed, or cottonseed meal or hulls in carload lots for distribution among the purchasers for use and not sale pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-5-355; 
(8)	Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-5-356 for persons selling or introducing into the city agricultural products or livestock, including animal products, raised in this state when the sale and introduction are made by the producer of the product and the sale is made within ninety (90) days of the introduction of the product into the city; 
(9)	Depository institutions pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-6-932; or 
(10)	Any business where the levy of such occupation tax is prohibited by the laws of the state of Georgia or the United States.3 
(b)	The exemptions and limitations contained in this article shall not be construed to repeal or otherwise affect in any way any franchise fees, business taxes or other fees or taxes otherwise allowed by law.4 
(Ord. of 2-6-95)
2 See this statute regarding collection of an occupation tax from such businesses. 
3 See O.C.G.A. §§ 33-8-8 and 33-8-8.1 regarding taxation of insurance companies. Licensing and taxation of insurers should be covered by a separate ordinance. 
4 See Title 3 of the Official Code of Georgia. 
Sec. 16-76.8. - Evidence of state registration when required. 
    Each person who is licensed under Title 43 of the Official Code of Georgia Annotated by the examining boards of the secretary of state's office shall provide evidence of proper and current state licensure before any city occupation tax certificate or regulatory fee certificate may be issued. 
(Ord. of 2-6-95)
Sec. 16-76.9. - Evidence of qualification required if applicable. 
(a)	Any business required to obtain health permits, bonds, certificates of qualification, certificates of competency or any other regulatory matter shall first, before the issuance of an occupation tax certificate or a regulatory fee certificate, show evidence of such qualification. 
(b)	Any business required to submit an annual application for continuance of the business shall do so before the registration is issued. 
(Ord. of 2-6-95)
Sec. 16-76.10. - Filing returns; other information required or requested. 
(a)	On or before March 1 of each year, an individual, business or practitioner subject to this occupation tax ordinance shall file with the city clerk on a form approved by and available from the city a signed return attesting to the number of employees of such business or practitioner during the calendar year. 
(b)	Individuals, businesses and practitioners doing business in the city shall submit to the city clerk or make available within thirty (30) days such information as may be required or requested by the city to determine the applicability and amount of the occupation tax or regulatory fee or to facilitate levying or collection of the occupation tax and/or regulatory fee(s). 
(Ord. of 2-6-95)
Sec. 16-76.11. - Confidentiality. 
    Information provided by a business or practitioner to the city for the purpose of determining the applicability and amount of the occupation tax or levying or collecting the occupation tax is confidential and exempt from disclosure under Article 4 of Chapter 18 of Title 50 of the Official Code of Georgia. Such information may be provided to the governing authority of another local government for occupation tax purposes or pursuant to court order or for the purpose of collecting occupation tax or prosecution for failure or refusal to pay occupation tax. 
(Ord. of 2-6-95)
Sec. 16-76.12. - Date due; penalty. 
(a)	Any occupation tax or regulatory fee due pursuant to this article shall be due and payable annually on July 1. In the event that any person commences business or initially engages in a regulated activity in the city after July 1 in any year, the tax and/or fee shall be due and payable on the date of the commencement of the business or regulated activity. 
(b)	Any individual, business or practitioner subject to any occupation tax or regulatory fee imposed by this ordinance which is unpaid for ninety (90) days after the date on which payment was due shall be subject to a penalty of ten (10) percent of the tax or fee due. 
(Ord. of 2-6-95)
Sec. 16-76.13. - Enforcement; violations. 
(a)	It is the duty of the city clerk to administer and enforce the provisions of this article, to perform all functions necessary to administer and enforce this article and to summon violators of this article to appear before the municipal court. The city clerk may issue executions against individuals, businesses and practitioners for taxes and fees which are due and owing. 
(b)	The city clerk shall issue executions against individuals, businesses and practitioners for taxes and fees which are due and owing. Such executions shall bear interest at the rate authorized by O.C.G.A. § 48-2-40 or, if such statute should be repealed, one percent per month. The lien shall cover the property of the individual, business or practitioner liable for payment of the delinquent occupation tax or regulatory fee and become fixed as of the date and time the occupation tax or regulatory fee became delinquent. The execution shall be levied by city clerk of the city upon property of the delinquent tax or fee payer located in the city and sufficient property shall be advertised and sold to pay the amount of the execution, including penalty, interest and costs. All other proceedings in relation thereto shall be as provided by the Code and Charter of the city and the laws of Georgia. The defendants at execution shall have the rights of defense, by affidavit of illegality of the tax or otherwise as provided by the Charter of the city and the laws of Georgia in regard to tax executions. 
(c)	When a nulla bona entry has been entered upon an execution, the person against whom the entry is made shall not be allowed or entitled to have or collect any fees or charges whatever for services rendered after the entry of the nulla bona. If, at any time after the nulla bona entry has been made, the person against whom the execution issues pays the tax in full together with all interest and costs accrued on the tax, the person may collect any fees and charges due to such person as if such person had never defaulted in the payment of the tax. 
(d)	Individuals, businesses and practitioners who fail or refuse to pay any occupation tax or regulatory fee charged pursuant to this article shall be subject to the penalty provided in Code section 1-12. Each day after the 90th day from the date the tax is due and remains unpaid shall constitute a separate offense. 
(e)	Individuals, businesses and practitioners who fail or refuse to make a timely or truthful tax return or make available truthful and accurate information the city requests or requires for determining applicability or amount of occupation tax or regulatory fee, or for levying or collecting such occupation tax or regulatory fee shall be subject to suspension of the right to conduct business. 
(f)	All persons subject to the occupation tax or regulatory fee imposed by this ordinance shall be required to file for and pay such tax or fee. For failure to do so, any officers or agents soliciting for or obtaining such person business shall be subject to the same penalty as other persons, businesses or practitioners who fail to obtain make a return for or pay the applicable occupation tax or regulatory fee. 
(Ord. of 2-6-95)
Sec. 16-76.14. - Public hearing. 
    After July 1, 1996, the city shall conduct at least one public hearing before adopting any ordinance or resolution which will increase the occupation tax rate specified in section(s) 16-76.4. 
(Ord. of 2-6-95)
Sec. 16-76.15. - Prior ordinance. 
    To the extent that any occupation taxes or regulatory fees are owed pursuant to an ordinance passed prior to this one, such amounts remain due and owing and the provisions of that prior ordinance will remain in effect with respect to such unpaid occupation taxes or regulatory fees until such time as they are paid in full. 
(Ord. of 2-6-95)
Sec. 16-76.16. - Severability. 
    In the event any portion of this article shall be declared or adjudged invalid or unconstitutional, it is the intention of the board of commissioners of the City of Hawkinsville that such adjudication shall in no manner affect the other sections, sentences, clauses or phrases of this ordinance which shall remain in full force and effect as if the invalid or unconstitutional section, sentence, clause or phrase were not originally part of the article. 
(Ord. of 2-6-95)
Secs. 16-77-16-95. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - PAWNBROKERS[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
State Law reference- Pawnbrokers, O.C.G.A. § 44-12-121 et seq.

Sec. 16-96. - Licensing requirements. 
    Each person engaging in the business of pawnbroker, or conducting a pawnbroking shop, in the city shall make a report to the chief of police before 12:00 noon each Monday of every article or thing pawned, whether such purchase is unconditional, or with the privilege of redeeming on the part of the seller. Such report shall specify the article or thing, giving a full description thereof, such as number, mark and other details as will make identification of such article or thing clear and positive. Each person aforesaid shall hold his shop subject to visitation and inspection by the police, and on refusal of any pawnbroker at any time to submit to such visitations or inspections, his shop shall be immediately closed by the chief of police. Any person who purchased jewelry, guns, pistols, household effects or other articles of merchandise or personal property, and at the time hereof gives the seller the privilege of redeeming same thereafter, shall be held and deemed a pawnbroker within the intent and meaning of this section. All licenses issued to pawnbrokers are subject to these provisions, any violations of which shall be punished by a revocation of the same and a fine up to one hundred dollars ($100.00); and no license for pawnbrokers shall be transferred from the person or firm to whom it was issued and no license shall be issued for less than an amount determined by the board of commissioners from time to time and listed in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the city clerk's office. 
(Ord. of 8-12-86)
Sec. 16-97. - Sales of goods other than pledged goods. 
    Pawnbrokers selling goods other than those pledged must pay an additional license. 
(Ord. of 8-12-86)
Sec. 16-98. - Buyers of secondhand clothing for resale. 
    Any person buying secondhand clothing for resale shall make a report every Monday to the police department as provided in the case of pawnbrokers. 
(Ord. of 8-12-86)
Secs. 16-99-16-115. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - PEDDLERS AND SOLICITORS[6] 
Footnotes: 
--- (6) --- 
State Law reference- Georgia Charitable Solicitations Act of 1988, O.C.G.A. § 43-17-1 et seq.; Transient Merchant Act of Georgia, O.C.G.A. § 43-46-1 et seq.; peddlers and itinerant traders, O.C.G.A. § 43-32-1 et seq.

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 16-116. - Organizations soliciting membership-Permit required. 
    Before any person shall solicit membership for any organization, union or society of any sort which requires from its members the payments of membership fees or dues or is entitled to make assessments against its members, such person shall make application in writing to the board of commissioners for the issuance of a permit to solicit members in such organization from among the citizens of the city or among employees of any businesses located in the city. 
(Code 1969, § 13-4)
Sec. 16-117. - Same-Permit application. 
    The application specified in section 16-116 shall give the name and nature of the organization for which the applicant desires to solicit members, whether such organization is incorporated or unincorporated, the location of its principal office and place of business and the names of its officers, along with the date of its organization, and its assets and liabilities. The application shall contain the age and residence of the applicant including places of residence of the applicant for the past ten (10) years, as well as the business or profession in which the applicant has been engaged during that time. The applicant shall furnish at least three (3) persons as reference to applicant's character. The application shall also include information as to whether the applicant is a salaried employee of the organization for which he is soliciting members, and what compensation, if any, he receives for obtaining members. 
(Code 1969, § 13-5)
Sec. 16-118. - Same-Hearing on permit application. 
    The application specified in section 16-116 shall be submitted to a regular meeting of the board of commissioners. If it is desired by the board to investigate further the information given in the application, or if the applicant desires a formal hearing on the application, the hearing shall be set for a time not later than the next regular meeting of the board. At the hearing the applicant may submit for consideration any evidence that he may desire bearing on the application, and any interested person shall have the right of appearing and giving evidence to the contrary. 
(Code 1969, § 13-6)
Sec. 16-119. - Same-Board consideration of application. 
    In passing upon the application for a permit to solicit membership in an organization the board of commissioners shall consider the character of the applicant, the nature of the business of the organization for which members are desired to be solicited, and its effect upon the general welfare of citizens of the city. 
(Code 1969, § 13-7)
Sec. 16-120. - Same-Granting or denying permit. 
    The granting or refusing to grant a permit to solicit membership in an organization shall be determined by vote of the board of commissioners, after consideration and hearing if same is requested by applicant or the board, in the same manner as other matters are so granted or denied by the vote of the board. 
(Code 1969, § 13-8)
Sec. 16-121. - Same-Permit or license fee; operation without permit. 
(a)	The permit specified in section 16-116, if the board of commissioners votes to grant it, shall be issued on payment of a permit or license fee in an amount to be determined by the board of commissioners from time to time and listed in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the city clerk's office. The term of the permit or license shall be for a term of one (1) year. 
(b)	It shall be unlawful for any person to solicit membership in an organization without having a valid current permit or license. 
(Code 1969, § 13-9)
Sec. 16-122. - Definition. 
    The term "solicitor" for the purposes of this division is defined to be any person who goes from house to house or from place to place in the city selling or taking orders for or offering to sell or take orders for, goods, wares or merchandise or any other article for present or future delivery. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. I, § 1)
Sec. 16-123. - License required. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to act as a solicitor without first securing a license to do so from the city clerk. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. I, § 2)
Sec. 16-124. - License application; bond. 
    Any person desiring a license to engage in the business of soliciting within the city shall make application therefor to the city clerk, stating the name and address of the applicant, the name and address of the person he represents and the kinds of goods offered for sale or the kind of services to be performed. Such applications shall be accompanied by a bond in the penal sum of an amount to be determined by the board of commissioners from time to time and listed in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the city clerk's office, executed by a surety company or by two (2) responsible freeholders residing in the city, or in lieu thereof a cash bond of equal amount conditioned upon the making of final delivery of the goods ordered or services to be performed, in accordance with the terms of such order, or, failing therein, that the advance payment of such order be refunded. Any person aggrieved by the action of such solicitor shall have a right of action on the bond for recovery of money or damages, or both. Such bond shall remain in full force and effect, and, in the case of a cash deposit, such deposit shall be retained by the city for a period of ninety (90) days after the expiration of any such license, unless sooner released by the board of commissioners. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. I, § 3)
Sec. 16-125. - Transfer of license. 
    Any permit issued under this division shall be nontransferable. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. IV)
Sec. 16-126. - Specifications for orders taken. 
    All orders taken by licensed solicitors shall be in writing, in duplicate, stating the terms thereof, and the amount paid in advance, if any, and one (1) copy shall be given to the purchaser. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. I, § 4)
Sec. 16-127. - Payment of license tax. 
    Nothing contained in this division shall affect in any manner the schedule of fees and charges of the city, which provides for the payment of a license tax for every itinerant trader and solicitor within the city. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. I, § 5)
Secs. 16-128-16-145. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - SOLICITATION FOR MAGAZINE SUBSCRIPTIONS 

Sec. 16-146. - Permit required. 
    No person shall solicit or take, or cause or instigate the solicitation or taking of subscriptions or orders for or sell or cause or instigate the sale of magazines within the corporate limits of the city, without first obtaining from the city clerk a permit to do so, after satisfying reasonable requirements to evidence good character. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. II, § 1)
Sec. 16-147. - Permit fee. 
    A permit fee or charge in an amount to be determined by the board of commissioners from time to time and listed in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the city clerk's office for every person affected by this division shall be paid as a condition to the grant of any permit hereunder, such permit charge and fee not being for revenue purposes, but to defray, in part, the cost of administering and enforcing the provisions of this division. The permit fee herein referred to shall be paid to the city clerk for the account of the city. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. II, § 2)
Sec. 16-148. - Revocation of permit. 
    The permit issued under this division shall be subject to revocation for just cause at any time by the city manager or by the board of commissioners, and when so revoked the holder thereof and any and all persons acting pursuant to its terms shall, as to further acts, be subjected to the terms of this division to the same extent as if the permit had never been obtained, except that the holder may apply and show cause for reinstatement of such revoked permit without the necessity of paying an additional permit fee and charge. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. II, § 3)
Sec. 16-149. - Appeals. 
    If application for a permit under this division or reinstatement of revoked permit is made to and refused by the city manager, any applicant may appeal the decision of the city manager to the board of commissioners. If application for issue of a permit or for reinstatement of a revoked permit is made to the board, the action of the board shall be final. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. II, § 4)
Sec. 16-150. - Applicability to licensed firms. 
    The provisions of this division shall not apply to firms, establishments or corporations or the employees of such where such firm, establishment or corporation has a current license from the city to do business within the city. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. II, § 6)
Sec. 16-151. - Violations. 
    Any person who violates any provision of this division or who obtains a permit or permits provided hereby by means of false information or representation shall be guilty of an offense under this division and shall upon conviction therefor in the municipal court be punished as provided by the Charter and this Code for violations of the ordinances of the city. Each day's violation of any provision of this division shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. II, § 5)
Secs. 16-152-16-170. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - CHARITABLE SOLICITATIONS 

Sec. 16-171. - Permit required. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person or for any agent, member, employee or representative thereof, directly or indirectly, to solicit property or financial assistance of any kind, to sell or offer to sell any article, tag, service emblem, publication, ticket, advertisement, subscription or anything of value, on the plea or the representation that such sale or solicitation or the proceeds thereof are for a charitable, educational, religious, patriotic or philanthropic purpose, on the streets, in any office or business building, by house-to-house canvass or in any other public or private place, or by telephone, mail or personal solicitation or in any other way in the city, unless such person has first obtained from the city clerk a permit to do so; provided, however, that the provisions of this section do not apply to any of the above-named persons where such solicitations or sales are made by the members thereof to members thereof without remuneration to the solicitor, or where such solicitation or sales occur upon property owned, leased, controlled or occupied by such person. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. III, § 1)
Sec. 16-172. - Permit application. 
    Any person desiring to do any of the acts detailed in section 16-171 shall first make a written application for a permit to do so to the city clerk. The application shall contain the following information: 
(1)	The name of the organization applying for a permit to solicit and its address;
(2)	The names and addresses of its principal officers and management;
(3)	The purpose for which any receipts derived from such solicitation are to be used;
(4)	The name of the person by whom the receipts of such solicitation shall be disbursed;
(5)	The name and address of the person who will be in direct charge of conducting the solicitation; 
(6)	An outline of the method or methods to be used in conducting the solicitation;
(7)	The time when such solicitations shall be made, giving the proposed dates for the beginning and the end of such solicitations; 
(8)	The amount of any wages, fees, commissions, expenses or emoluments to be expended or paid to anyone in connection with such solicitation, together with the manner in which such wages, fees, expenses, commissions or emoluments are to be expended, to whom paid, and the amount thereof. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. III, § 2)
Sec. 16-173. - Investigation of application. 
    Upon the filing of an application for a permit under this division, the chief of police shall immediately make an investigation to determine the truth or falsity of the recitals in the application and if he determines that any of the material statements of fact are false, he shall so notify the city clerk and a permit shall not issue. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. III, § 3)
Sec. 16-174. - Denial of permit; appeals. 
    Upon refusal to grant a permit under this division, the city clerk shall notify the applicant in writing and within ten (10) days thereof the applicant may file a petition with the board of commissioners to review the decision of the city clerk, and the decision of the board shall be subject to review in the same manner as other decisions of the board relating to the issuance of licenses. 
(Ord. of 4-12-77, art. III, § 4)
ARTICLE VIII. - MISCELLANEOUS 

Sec. 16-175. - Refund of erroneously or illegally assessed or collected taxes and license fees. 
(a)	The City of Hawkinsville may refund to taxpayers any and all taxes and license fees which are determined to have been erroneously or illegally assessed and collected from taxpayers of the City of Hawkinsville under the laws of the State of Georgia or under the resolutions or ordinances of the City of Hawkinsville or which have been determined to have been voluntarily or involuntarily overpaid by the taxpayers. 
(b)	In any occasion which it is determined that an erroneous or illegal collection of any tax or license fee has been paid by the City of Hawkinsville or that a taxpayer has voluntarily or involuntarily overpaid any tax or license fee, the taxpayer from whom the tax or license fee was collected may file a claim for a refund with the City of Hawkinsville at any time within one (1) year or, in the case of taxes, three (3) years after the date of the payment of the tax or license fee to the City of Hawkinsville. The claim for refund shall be in writing and shall be in the form and shall contain the information required by the City of Hawkinsville. The claim shall include a summary statement of the grounds upon which the taxpayer relies. In the event the taxpayer desires a conference or hearing before the Board of Commissioners of the City of Hawkinsville in connection with any claim for a refund, such taxpayer shall so specify in writing in the claim if the claim conforms to the requirement of this section, the Board of Commissioners of the City of Hawkinsville shall grant a conference at a time specified by it. The Board of Commissioners of the City of Hawkinsville shall consider information contained in the taxpayer's claim for a refund and such other information as is available. The Board of Commissioners of the City of Hawkinsville shall approve or disapprove the taxpayer's claim and shall notify the taxpayer of this action. In the event any claim for refund is approved, the Board of Commissioners of the City of Hawkinsville shall proceed under the immediately preceding paragraph of this section to give effect to the terms of the preceding paragraph. No refund provided for in this section shall be assignable. 
(c)	Any taxpayer whose claim for refund is denied by the Board of Commissioners of the City of Hawkinsville or whose claim is not denied or approved by the Board of Commissioners of the City of Hawkinsville within one (1) year from the date of filing of the claim shall have the right to bring an action for refund in the Superior Court of Pulaski County, Georgia. No action or proceeding for the recovery of a refund shall be commenced before the expiration of one (1) year from the date of filing the claim for refund unless the Board of Commissioners of the City of Hawkinsville renders a decision on the claim within the one-year period. No action or proceeding for the recovery of a refund shall be commenced after the expiration of one year from the date the claim is denied. The one-year period prescribed in this paragraph for filing an action for a refund shall be extended for such period as may be agreed upon in writing between the taxpayer and the Board of Commissioners of the City of Hawkinsville during the one-year or any extension of the one-year period. 
(d)	All refunds approved or allowed under this section shall be paid from funds of the City of Hawkinsville to which taxes or license fees were originally paid. The funds shall be paid within sixty (60) days of the approval of the taxpayer's claim or within sixty (60) days of the entry of a final decision in any action for a refund. 
(e)	The Board of Commissioners of the City of Hawkinsville may by ordinance adopt rules and regulations governing the administration of this section and may delegate the administration of this section, including the approval or disapproval of claims where the reason for the claim is based on an obvious clerical error to an appropriate department or official of the City of Hawkinsville. In disputed cases where there is no obvious error, the approval or disapproval of claims may not be delegated by the Board of Commissioners of the City of Hawkinsville. 
(Ord. of 4-4-01)
Sec. 16-176. - Hotel-motel tax. 
(a)	Imposed. Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-13-51 et seq. there is hereby levied an excise tax in the amount of five (5) percent of the charge to the public for furnishing for value to the public of any room or rooms, lodging, or accommodations furnished by any person or legal entity licensed by, or required to pay business or occupational taxes to the City of Hawkinsville, for operating a hotel, motel, inn, lodge, tourist camp, tourist cabin or any other place in which rooms, lodging, or accommodations are regularly furnished for value. 
(b)	Collection. Any and all monies collected from the levy of said tax shall be expressly and exclusively used in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 48-13-51(a)(3), to enhance and expand the economy of Hawkinsville and Pulaski County through the promotion of tourism. 
    The City of Hawkinsville shall contract with Hawkinsville-Pulaski County Chamber of Commerce to carry out an aggressive tourism program and shall commit all proceeds from the levy of the hotel-motel tax and other designated funds for this express and exclusive purpose. 
    The Clerk of the City of Hawkinsville shall collect the proceeds from the levy of the hotel-motel tax and remit same to Hawkinsville-Pulaski County Chamber of Commerce on behalf of the City of Hawkinsville, said collection and remittance being provided at no charge. 
    The proceeds from the levy of the hotel-motel tax shall be collected monthly no later than the 20th of the month following the month of collection. 
(c)	Reporting; audit. The Executive Director of the Hawkinsville-Pulaski County Chamber of Commerce shall publish the minutes of all meetings, maintain a full accounting of all funds, publish not less than quarterly a report of activities and financial statement to the members of the board of the City of Hawkinsville and the Hawkinsville-Pulaski County Chamber of Commerce shall cause an annual audit of the funds of the board by a certified public accountant licensed to perform said services in the State of Georgia. 
(Ord. of 2-13-90, §§ I-VI; Ord. of 11-6-06, §§ 1-3)
Secs. 16-177-16-179. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IX. - TRANSIENT MERCHANTS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 16-180. - Short title. 
    This article may be cited as the "City of Hawkinsville Transient Merchant Ordinance." 
(Ord. No. 2011-1, 2-7-11)
Sec. 16-181. - Transient merchant defined. 
    As used in this article, the term "transient merchant" means any person, firm, or corporation, as principal or agent, or both, which is not a regular retail or wholesale merchant with a permanent place of business in the city, but rather one who displays samples, model goods, wares or merchandise in or upon any lot, building, room or structure of any kind, whether fixed or mobile, for the purpose of securing orders for the retail sale of such items of like kind or quality for immediate or future delivery. The term "transient merchant" shall not include any person who: 
(1)	Sells harvested but unprocessed agricultural or forestry products;
(2)	Makes house-to-house or personal calls for the purpose of displaying samples or taking orders for shipment directly from a manufacturer; 
(3)	Conducts business at any industry or association trade show;
(4)	Sells items at a rummage, garage, antique or similar sale when the net proceeds of such sale are to be used for charitable or benevolent purposes; 
(5)	Sells items from the home of a resident of the city, provided such business activity otherwise complies with city ordinances; or 
(6)	Sells items at an organized show or exhibition held within the corporate limits of the city by a person who has first obtained from the city a license for the purpose of conducting such show or exhibition. 
(Ord. No. 2011-1, 2-7-11)
Sec. 16-182. - Compliance with state law. 
    No transient merchant shall engage in business in the city without complying with all applicable provisions of state law. 
(Ord. No. 2011-1, 2-7-11)
Sec. 16-183. - Registered agents for receipt of process, notice or demands generally; serving process, notice or demands on registered agent. 
(a)	No transient merchant shall engage in business in the city until he has filed the name and permanent address of his registered agent with the city clerk. 
(b)	Such registered agent shall be a resident of the city and shall be the landowner upon whose property the transient merchant is intending to transact his business, if such landowner is also a resident of the city. If the landowner is not a resident of the city, then such registered agent shall be any other bona fide resident of the city who is over the age of eighteen (18) and sui juris. Such agent may be served with any process, notice or demand required or permitted by law to be served upon the transient merchant, in the same manner provided by law for the service of a summons and complaint. 
(c)	Such registered agent shall agree in writing to act as such agent and a copy of the agreement shall be filed with the license application. 
(d)	The city clerk shall maintain an alphabetical record of all transient merchants and the names and addresses of their registered agents. 
(e)	Nothing contained in this section shall limit or affect the right to serve any process, notice or demand in any other manner permitted by law. 
(Ord. No. 2011-1, 2-7-11)
DIVISION 2. - APPLICATION TO TRANSACT BUSINESS; REGULATORY FEE 

Sec. 16-184. - Application. 
(a)	Any transient merchant desiring to transact business within the city shall file with the city clerk an application prior to the transaction of any such business. Such application shall include the following information: 
(1)	The name and permanent address of the transient merchant;
(2)	The name and permanent address of the transient merchant's registered agent or office;
(3)	The type of business to be conducted;
(4)	The date and state of incorporation, if incorporated;
(5)	If a foreign corporation, the date the corporation became qualified to transact business in this state; 
(6)	The number of days during which the sale is to be conducted;
(7)	Evidence of either ownership of the property by the transient merchant or a written lease or written permission from the owner of the property to the transient merchant regarding the property upon which the sale is to be conducted; and 
(8)	The location where the sale is to be conducted.
(b)	No person shall make any false statements in any application in order to conduct a transient merchant's business. 
(Ord. No. 2011-1, 2-7-11)
Sec. 16-185. - Regulatory fee; change in location. 
(a)	There shall be a regulatory fee payable in conjunction with the occupational tax upon submittal of an approved application. Such fee shall be established by the city commission and the city manager shall be allowed to collect said fee upon submission of the application to transact business. 
(b)	Change in locations or renewals of existing locations will require a new application subject to the established regulatory fee. 
(Ord. No. 2011-1, 2-7-11)
Sec. 16-186. - Issuance; term; etc. 
    After the applicant has complied with all the provisions of this division, a transient business application shall be approved. Such approval is not transferable, is valid only within the territorial limits of the city, is valid only for the business stated on the application, and shall expire on the last day named therein on which the sale is to be conducted. 
(Ord. No. 2011-1, 2-7-11)
Chapter 17 - TRAFFIC[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Municipal court, § 10; offenses, Ch. 11; police, Ch. 12; streets and sidewalks, Ch. 15.
State Law reference- Authority to provide devices to control the flow of traffic, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III; Uniform Rules of the Road, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-1 et seq.; power of local authorities generally, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-371; adoption of uniform rules of the road by local authorities, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-372; prosecution of traffic offenses, O.C.G.A. § 40-13-1 et seq.

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 17-1. - Speed limit generally. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to drive any motorcycle, automobile, truck or other motor vehicle, or bicycle, on any street within the city at a greater speed than twenty-five (25) miles per hour, except as follows: 
(1)	The lawful rate of speed within any school zone properly designated by appropriate signs shall not be in excess of twenty (20) miles per hour. 
(2)	Where no special hazards exist the chief of police may by appropriate signs or markers designate speed zones in excess of the twenty-five (25) miles per hour limitation, but in no case may the limit be in excess of forty-five (45) miles per hour. 
(Code 1969, § 17-1)
Sec. 17-2. - Bicycle lights. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to run any bicycle within the city after sunset and before sunrise without having one (1) or more headlights, properly lighted on such vehicle. 
(Code 1969, § 17-3)
Sec. 17-3. - Riding bicycle on sidewalk. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to ride a bicycle on any sidewalk of the city. 
(Code 1969, § 17-7)
Sec. 17-4. - Parking within marked space. 
    Where parking spaces or areas are marked or lined on the streets, vehicles shall be parked entirely within the spaces or areas as indicated. 
(Code 1969, § 17-4)
Sec. 17-5. - Parking near fire hydrant. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to leave standing any vehicle of any kind or character on the streets of the city within ten (10) feet of a fire hydrant. 
(Code 1969, § 17-5)
Sec. 17-6. - Right-of-way of fire vehicles. 
    All fire vehicles belonging to the fire department shall have the right-of-way in, to and over the streets of the city in going to and returning from a fire alarm. It shall be the duty of all persons driving other vehicles to clear the center of the street for the fire vehicles. 
(Code 1969, § 17-8)
Sec. 17-7. - Keeping vehicle in proper lane. 
(a)	All drivers of vehicles shall keep to the right side of the street, except where otherwise permitted on one-way streets. 
(b)	In order that all vehicles on each side of the street shall be headed in the same direction, owners, drivers or agents of vehicles are required to turn, if necessary, when stopping at sidewalk, so that the sidewalk will be to the right of such driver when stop is made. 
(c)	U-turns are prohibited.
(Code 1969, § 17-9)
Sec. 17-8. - Truck routes established. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for anyone to operate a motor vehicle or truck, with ten (10) wheels or more on the vehicle, except on streets designated by the city or the state department of transportation as being thoroughfares to be used for intercity transit by such motor vehicles. Such vehicles may, however, travel on city streets if the vehicle's departure or destination point is in the city. 
(b)	The permissible routes through the city for such vehicles for intercity transit are from the Highway 341 Bypass east to Broad Street, along Broad Street to South Jackson Street; along Broad Street east to the Ocmulgee River Bridge (Roger H. Lawson Memorial Bridge); west from the Ocmulgee River Bridge (Roger H. Lawson Memorial Bridge) onto Florida Avenue to Broad Street and along Broad Street west; west from the Ocmulgee River Bridge (Roger H. Lawson Memorial Bridge) and right onto North Houston Street to Second Street and right onto Progress Avenue. 
(Ord. of 8-14-84)
Sec. 17-9. - Large motor vehicles and/or trailers; prohibited. 
(a)	No motor vehicle which has more than ten (10) wheels or any motor vehicle and trailer which contain in the aggregate more than ten (10) wheels may travel upon, across, over, or through Sixth Street in the City of Hawkinsville, Georgia, from the intersection of Sixth Street with Progress Avenue through the eastward terminus of Sixth Street. 
(b)	Any violation of this section is punishable by a fine not exceeding one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) or imprisonment for six (6) months or both such fine and imprisonment or such other alternative sentencing as the municipal court shall deem just and proper. 
(Ord. of 7-16-97)
Editor's note- Ord. No. 97-10, adopted July 16, 1997, was not specifically amendatory of the Code, hence; inclusion as § 17-9 was at the discretion of the editor. 
Secs. 17-10-17-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - TRAFFIC SCHEDULES 

Sec. 17-26. - Definition. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Traffic schedule means the official list or schedule of the regulation compiled by the city and maintained in the city clerk's office for the following purposes: 
(1)	Designation of the location of traffic-control devices;
(2)	Designation of areas or zones where regulations are applied to parking, loading, bus stops or taxicab stands; 
(3)	Establishment of speed limits;
(4)	Restriction or regulation of traffic at certain times on certain streets or to certain types, weights or sizes of vehicles; 
(5)	Designation of the location of through streets, stop intersections, yield-right-of-way intersections, waiting lanes, one-way streets or truck traffic routes; and 
(6)	Establishment of regulations upon vehicle turns at designated locations.
Sec. 17-27. - Stop intersections. 
    Stop intersections shall be as established and posted in the traffic schedule. 
(Mo. of 2-10-87; Mo. of 2-24-87; Mo. of 12-13-88)
Sec. 17-28. - No parking areas. 
    The areas designated on the traffic schedule may not be used for the parking of motor vehicles or obstructed in any manner for the purpose of leaving clear vision for traffic. No vehicle or instrument of transportation shall stop or park at any time in any zone or space designated and marked as a no parking zone or space. All no parking zones and spaces shall be marked and designated by yellow paint or by appropriate signs. 
(Ord. of 2-26-74; Ord. of 8-9-77, §§ I, II; Mo. of 1-8-80; Mo. of 7-27-82; Ord. of 8-27-85) 
Sec. 17-29. - Limited time parking areas. 
    Parking zones are hereby ordained and established for and upon the streets of the city and listed on the traffic schedule. 
(1)	Fifteen-minute parking zones: No vehicle or instrument of transportation shall stop or park in any fifteen-minute parking zone or space for any single, interrupted period greater than fifteen (15) minutes. All fifteen-minute parking zones and spaces shall be designated and marked by brown paint or by appropriate signs. There shall be established and marked by the city manager certain fifteen-minute parking zones and spaces. 
(2)	Thirty-minute parking zones: No vehicle or instrument of transportation shall park or stop in any thirty-minute parking zone or space for any single, uninterrupted period greater than thirty (30) minutes. All thirty-minute parking zones and spaces shall be marked by green paint or by appropriate signs. There shall be established and marked by the city manager certain thirty-minute parking zones and spaces. 
(3)	Two-hour parking zones: No vehicle or instrument of transportation shall park or stop in any two-hour parking zone or space for any single, uninterrupted period greater than two (2) hours. All two-hour parking zones or spaces shall be designated and marked by blue paint or by appropriate signs. There shall be established and marked by the city manager certain two-hour parking zones and spaces. 
(4)	Eight-hour parking zones: No vehicle or instrument of transportation shall park or stop in any eight-hour parking zone or space for any single, uninterrupted period greater than eight (8) hours. All eight-hour parking zones and spaces shall be designated and marked by white paint or by appropriate signs. 
(Ord. of 8-9-77, §§ I, II)
Sec. 17-30. - Speed zones. 
    Speed zones shall be as established and posted in the traffic schedule. 
(Ord. of 4-25-73; Ord. of 6-14-78; Ord. of 7-25-78; Ord. of 2-10-87; Ord. of 5-12-87; Ord. of 10-11-83; Ord. of 10-3-94) 
Sec. 17-31. - U-turns. 
    No vehicle shall be turned so as to proceed in the opposite direction upon any street, road, highway or alley or other way designed or used for vehicular traffic in the City of Hawkinsville, Georgia. 
(Ord. of 2-21-95)
Chapter 18 - UTILITIES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference- Administration, Ch. 2; buildings and building regulations, Ch. 5; wells, § 9-26 et seq.; obstructing drainage ways, § 11-12; solid waste management, Ch. 14; streets and sidewalks, Ch. 15.
State Law reference- Power of city or county to provide stormwater, sewerage collection and disposal systems, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(6); dumping certain wastes in storm or sanitary sewers prohibited, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-2; Solid Waste Management Act, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-20 et seq.; adoption of ordinances, rules and regulations relating to payment for street improvements and construction of water, gas and sewer connections, payment of costs of connections, O.C.G.A. § 36-39-7; city's authority to acquire, construct, extend, operate, maintain and collect fees for water and sewage systems, O.C.G.A. § 36-34-5; Resource Recovery Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-63-1 et seq.; grants of state funds to municipal corporations for public purposes, O.C.G.A. § 36-40-20 et seq.; executions for collection of assessments for laying sewers, O.C.G.A. § 48-5-358.

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 18-1. - Definition. 
    For the purposes of this chapter, the word "utility" shall be construed to mean and include water, sewer and/or any other utility service furnished by the city to consumers thereof. 
Sec. 18-2. - Scope. 
    All pertinent provisions of this chapter are hereby made a part of the terms and conditions whereby the city shall furnish any utility service to any person, or whereby the city shall make any utility connections, or perform any work of any kind in connection with the furnishing of any utility service pursuant to the rules and regulations of the city. 
Sec. 18-3. - Service to comply with technical provisions. 
    Any utility service furnished under the provisions of this chapter shall be in accordance with and in compliance with all applicable technical provisions of this Code, state law and city ordinances, rules and regulations. 
Sec. 18-4. - Rules, regulations. 
    The board of commissioners shall have the authority to establish by rule or regulation such standards and specifications as may be deemed necessary for the installation, construction and maintenance of any utility service system owned and operated by the city within or without the city and under the management of the city. Such rules, regulations, standards and specifications shall be filed in the office of the city manager. Violation of such rules, regulations, standards and specifications shall be deemed an offense. 
Sec. 18-5. - Right of entry. 
    Any authorized inspector of the city shall have free access at any time to all premises supplied with any utility service by the city for the purpose of examination in order to protect the utility services from abusive use. 
Sec. 18-6. - Termination of service. 
    The city shall have the right to disconnect or refuse to connect or reconnect any utility service for any of the following reasons: 
(1)	Failure to meet the applicable provisions of law;
(2)	Violation of the rules and regulations pertaining to utility service;
(3)	Nonpayment of bills;
(4)	Willful or negligent waste of service due to improper or imperfect pipes, fixtures, appliances or otherwise; 
(5)	Molesting any meter, seal or other equipment controlling or regulating the supply of utility service; 
(6)	Theft or diversion and/or use of service without payment therefor;
(7)	Vacancy of premises.
Sec. 18-7. - City not liable for damage. 
    The city shall not be liable for any damage to any customer of any utility service furnished by the city due to backflow of the sewerage system, failure of supply, interruption of service or any other cause outside the direct control of the city. 
Sec. 18-8. - Utility service-Application required. 
    Any person desiring any utility service furnished by the city shall make application for the same to the city. The application shall contain the applicant's name, address and the uses for which such utility service is desired. 
Sec. 18-9. - Same-Not available to debtors. 
    The city may decline or fail or cease to furnish utility service to any person who may be in debt to the city for any reason. 
Sec. 18-10. - Same-Use assumed. 
    All premises connected to any utility service of the city shall be assumed to be using such utility service and the owner or occupant shall be charged therefor so long as such premises remains connected with the utility service. 
Sec. 18-11. - Damaging, injuring, or interfering with property of utilities. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person intentionally and without authority to injure or destroy any meter, pipe, conduit, wire, line, post, lamp, manhole cover, fireplug, trash or garbage container or any accessories thereto or used by or belonging to the City of Hawkinsville, or to any public or private utility or company engaged in the manufacture or sale of electricity, gas, water, telephone, the furnishing of sanitary sewer service, collection of garbage and/or trash, or other public services; intentionally and without authority to prevent a meter from properly registering the quantity of such service supplied; in any way to interfere with the proper action of the City of Hawkinsville, such public or private utility or company; intentionally to divert any services of the City of Hawkinsville, or such public or private utility or company; or otherwise intentionally and without authority to use or cause to be used, without the consent of the City of Hawkinsville, or such public or private utility or company, any service manufactured, sold, or distributed by the City of Hawkinsville, such public or private utility or company. 
(b)	Where there is no evidence to the contrary, the person performing any of the illegal acts set forth in subsection (a) of this Code section and the person who with knowledge of such violation receives the benefit of such service without proper charge as a result of the improper action shall be presumed to be responsible for the act of tampering or diversion. 
(c)	Every person convicted in the municipal court of the City of Hawkinsville of a violation of any provision of subsection (a) or (b) hereof shall be punished as provided in section 1-12 of this Code. 
(Ord. of 2-25-95)
State Law reference- Damaging, injuring or interfering with property of public utility companies, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-25. 
Sec. 18-12. - Temporary interruption of service. 
    The city reserves the right to cut off any utility service without notice in case of emergency. When an interruption in service is necessary for the maintenance and improvement of the utility system, affected customers will be notified as circumstances permit. 
Sec. 18-13. - Restricting use. 
    The city hereby reserves the right to at any time restrict or prevent the use of any utility service furnished by the city during periods of emergency or circumstances demanding such restriction or prevention of use. 
Sec. 18-14. - Resale of service by customer. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to resell to others any utility service obtained from the city except only by special arrangement with the city manager. 
Sec. 18-15. - Connections to service. 
    Connections for any utility service furnished by the city shall be made only under the supervision of the building inspector. 
Sec. 18-16. - Separate connections. 
    Every building, structure or consumer in the city shall have a separate utility service connection except only by special arrangement with the city manager. 
Sec. 18-17. - Unlawful connections. 
    Any person who makes any connection in any manner to any utility system, whether owned by the city or not, without the prior knowledge and consent of the owner of such utility system shall be deemed guilty of an offense. 
Sec. 18-18. - Unlawful use. 
    No person other than employees of the city shall be authorized to connect, turn on, turn off or disconnect any utility service offered by the city, or remove, replace or repair any equipment connected to any such utility service. 
Sec. 18-19. - Maintenance of system by consumer. 
    The consumer of any utility service furnished by the city shall maintain and keep in good repair all connections, appliances and other apparatus installed and used in connection with such utility service. 
Secs. 18-20-18-35. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - WATER 

Sec. 18-36. - Authority for tap, extension. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to tap to or extend any water main or use water with or without a meter, or to have a waterline for use, whether within or without the city, except by authority of the city. 
Sec. 18-37. - Meters and appurtenances from street through meter box. 
    The water meter and all appurtenances from the street through the meter box shall belong to and remain the property of the city, and no refunds shall be made in connection with any installations. 
Sec. 18-38. - Water department to control meters. 
    All water meters shall be under the exclusive control of the water department, and all repairs and inspections shall be made only by the water department. No one but an authorized employee of the water department shall be allowed to put in, take out or in any way handle the meters. 
Sec. 18-39. - Service charge for meter taps. 
(a)	All water meter taps shall be made and installed on the basis of a nonrefundable service charge, which shall be an amount determined by the board of commissioners from time to time and listed in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the clerk's office. 
(b)	If it is necessary to cut the street pavement in order to make a water tap, a charge in an amount determined by the board of commissioners from time to time and listed in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the city clerk's office in addition to the charge specified in subsection (a) will be made for the purpose of paying for repaving the pavement. 
Sec. 18-40. - Water rates. 
    Monthly rates shall be charged for all water service customers in an amount determined by the board of commissioners from time to time and listed in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the clerk's office. 
Sec. 18-41. - Landlords responsible for payment. 
    Landlords and their agents shall be responsible for the water rents, and shall give the superintendent written notice of the nonuse of water. 
Sec. 18-42. - Deposits required. 
    A deposit in an amount determined by the board of commissioners from time to time and listed in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the clerk's office shall be required for residential and small commercial water customers of the city. 
Sec. 18-43. - Payment cycle. 
    All water bills shall be paid monthly. The city clerk shall furnish the superintendent of the waterworks on the tenth of each month a list of all persons who have not paid their water rents for that month, and it shall be the duty of the superintendent of the waterworks to cut off the water supply from such parties. Before the water shall be turned on, such parties shall present to the superintendent a receipt from the city clerk for the water rentals for that month, and a further sum in an amount determined by the board of commissioners from time to time and listed in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the clerk's office for turning the water on. 
(Code 1969, § 19-1)
Sec. 18-44. - Rents and tapping fee receipt prerequisite to turning water on. 
    The superintendent of waterworks shall not turn water on to any new work until the party desiring to use water from the same shall present to him a receipt from the city clerk for rents and tapping fees for the remainder of the month. 
(Code 1969, § 19-3)
Sec. 18-45. - Late payment penalty. 
    There is levied a charge upon the users of the water who do not pay their water bills in full by the tenth of the month following the month for which water was furnished and is owed for, an amount equal to ten (10) percent of the bill for such month. The amount shall be added to and be due and collectible as the basic water bill. 
(Code 1969, § 19-4)
Sec. 18-46. - Responsibility of owner of multiple dwelling. 
    The city shall furnish water to houses that are occupied by two (2) or more families only if the owner of the house, whether a dweller therein or not, is responsible for the water bill for water furnished the house and all occupants therein. 
(Code 1969, § 19-5)
Secs. 18-47-18-65. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - SEWERS 

Sec. 18-66. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    B.O.D. (denoting biochemical oxygen demand) means the quantity of oxygen utilized in the biochemical oxidation of organic matter under standard laboratory procedure in five (5) days at twenty (20) degrees Celsius (sixty-eight (68) degrees Fahrenheit) expressed in milligrams per liter. 
    Building drain means that part of the lowest horizontal piping of a drainage system which receives the discharge from soil, waste and other drainage pipes inside the walls of the building and conveys it to the building sewer, beginning five (5) feet outside the inner face of the building wall. 
    Building sewer means the extension from the building drain to the public sewer or other place of disposal. 
    Garbage means solid wastes from the preparation, cooking and disposing of food, and from the handling, storage and sale of produce. 
    Industrial wastes means the liquid wastes from industrial processes as distinct from sanitary sewage. 
    Natural outlet means any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake or other body of surface water or groundwater. 
    pH means the logarithm of the reciprocal of the hydrogen ion concentration in moles per liter. 
    Properly shredded garbage means the wastes from the preparation, cooking and dispensing of food that have been shredded to such degree that all particles will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally prevailing in public sewers, with no particle greater than one-half inch in any dimension. 
    Public sewer means a sewer in which all owners of abutting properties have equal rights and which is controlled by public authority. 
    Sanitary sewer means a sewer which carries sewage and to which stormwaters, surface waters and groundwaters are not intentionally admitted. 
    Sewage means a combination of the water-carried wastes from residences, business buildings, institutions and industrial establishments, together with such groundwaters, surface waters and stormwaters as may be present. 
    Sewage treatment plant means any arrangement of devices and structures or lagoons used for treating sewage presently owned or afterward acquired by this city. 
    Sewage works means all facilities for collecting, pumping, treating and disposing of sewage. 
    Sewer means a pipe or conduit for carrying sewage. 
    Storm sewer or storm drain means a sewer which carries stormwaters and surface waters and drainage, but excludes sewage and polluted industrial wastes. 
    Superintendent means the city manager, or his authorized deputy, agent or representative. 
    Suspended solids means solids that either float on the surface of or are in suspension in water, sewage or other liquids, and which are removable by laboratory filtering. 
    Watercourse means a channel in which a flow of water occurs, either continuously or intermittently. 
Sec. 18-67. - Power and authority of inspectors. 
    The city manager and other duly authorized employees of the city bearing proper credentials and identification shall be permitted to enter upon all properties for the purpose of inspection, observation, measurement, sampling and testing, in accordance with the provisions of this article. 
Sec. 18-68. - Deposit of objectionable wastes. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to place, deposit or permit to be deposited in an unsanitary manner upon public or private property within the city, or in any area under the jurisdiction of the city, any human or animal excrement, garbage or other objectionable waste. 
Sec. 18-69. - Discharges into natural outlets. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge or cause to be discharged to any natural outlet within the city, or in any area under the jurisdiction of the city, any sanitary sewage, industrial wastes or other polluted waters, except where suitable treatment has been provided in accordance with subsequent provisions of this article. 
Sec. 18-70. - Private disposal facilities. 
    Except as hereinafter provided, it shall be unlawful for any person to construct or maintain or cause to be constructed or maintained any privy, privy vault, septic tank, cesspool or other facility intended or used for the disposal of sewage. 
Sec. 18-71. - Damage to sewerage works. 
(a)	It shall be unlawful for any person to maliciously, willfully or negligently break, damage, destroy, uncover, deface or tamper with any structure, appurtenance or equipment which is a part of the city sewerage works. 
(b)	No unauthorized person shall place, insert, drop or allow to enter the sanitary or storm system, pipes, manholes or lift stations any debris, construction materials, wrappings, bindings, rope, wire, plastic, paper, lumber, shingles, bricks and similar materials or any other object which damage the sanitary or storm sewer system of the city. 
Sec. 18-72. - City water service required. 
    No tap shall be permitted with a public sewer unless the premises to be served thereby is served or to be served by the city water system through a water meter. 
Sec. 18-73. - Tapping fees. 
(a)	The fee for a four-inch tap to an existing sewer shall be an amount determined by the board of commissioners from time to time and listed in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the clerk's office. The fee for sewer taps over four (4) inches shall be on a cost-plus basis as established by the city manager. 
(b)	If it is necessary to cut the street pavement in order to make a sewer tap, a charge in addition to those named in subsection (a) will be made for the purpose of paying for repaving the pavement. Based on a ditch width minimum of twenty-four (24) inches, the charge will be an amount determined by the board of commissioners form time to time and listed in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the clerk's office for each square yard, or fraction thereof, of pavement removed. 
Sec. 18-74. - Sewer charges established. 
    There is hereby assessed and levied upon each parcel of real property in the city on which is located a sewer pipeline connected onto the sewer system of the city, and the owner, residents or tenants of same a monthly charge for the use and maintenance of the sewer system of the city. The rates in effect for sewage use shall be in an amount determined by the board of commissioners from time to time and listed in the schedule of fees and charges maintained in the clerk's office. 
Sec. 18-75. - Payment of charges; penalty. 
    Payment of sewer charges and penalties shall be as set forth in sections 18-43 through 18-46 for water charges. 
Sec. 18-76. - Interceptors. 
(a)	Grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be provided when in the opinion of the superintendent they are necessary for the proper handling of liquid wastes containing grease in excessive amounts, or any flammable wastes, sand and other harmful ingredients; except that such interceptors shall not be required for private living quarters or dwelling units. All interceptors shall be of a type and capacity approved by the superintendent and shall be located as to be readily and easily accessible for cleaning and inspection. 
(b)	Grease and oil interceptors shall be constructed of impervious materials capable of withstanding abrupt and extreme changes in temperature. They shall be of substantial construction, watertight and equipped with easily removable covers which, when bolted in place, shall be gastight and watertight. 
(c)	When installed, all grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be maintained by the owner, at his expense, in continuously efficient operation at all times. 
Sec. 18-77. - Certain wastes subject to review and approval. 
    The admission into the public sewers of any water wastes having: 
(1)	A five-day biochemical oxygen demand greater than three hundred (300) milligrams per liter; 
(2)	Containing more than three hundred fifty (350) milligrams per liter of suspended solids;
(3)	Containing any quantity of substance having the characteristics described in section 18-78; or 
(4)	Having an average daily flow greater than two (2) percent of the average daily flow of the city; 
shall be subject to the review and approval of the superintendent. 
Sec. 18-78. - Restricted discharges enumerated. 
    Except as herein provided, no person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any of the following described waters or wastes to any public sewer: 
(1)	Any liquid or vapor having a temperature higher than one hundred fifty (150) degrees Fahrenheit (sixty-six (66) degrees Celsius); 
(2)	Any waters or wastes which may contain more than one hundred (100) milligrams per liter of fat, oil or grease; 
(3)	Any gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil or other flammable or explosive liquid, solid or gas; 
(4)	Any garbage that has not been properly shredded;
(5)	Any ashes, cinders, sand, mud, straw, shavings, metal, glass, rags, feathers, tar, plastics, wood, paunch manure or any other solid or viscous substance capable of causing obstruction to the flow in sewers or other interference with the proper operation of the sewage works; 
(6)	Any waters or wastes having a pH lower than 5.5 or higher than 9.0, or having any other corrosive property capable of causing damage or hazard to structures, equipment and personnel of the sewage works; 
(7)	Any waters or wastes containing a toxic or poisonous substance in sufficient quantity to injure or interfere with any sewage treatment process, constitute a hazard to humans or animals, or create any hazard in the receiving waters of the sewage treatment plant. The fixed upper limits for the constituents listed below, in parts per million, shall be: 
a.Cadmium0.02b.Chromium1.0c.Copper1.0d.Cyanide0.2e.Nickel1.0f.Silver1.0g.Lead0.1h.Zinc3.0i.Phenol0.05j.Arsenic0.05 
(8)	Any waters or wastes containing suspended solids of such character and quantity that unusual attention or expense is required to handle such materials at the sewage treatment plant; 
(9)	Any noxious or malodorous gas or substance capable of creating a public nuisance.
Sec. 18-79. - Discharges into storm sewers, approved natural outlets. 
    Stormwater and all other unplatted drainage shall be discharged to such sewers as are specifically designated as storm sewers, or to a natural outlet approved by the superintendent. Industrial cooling water or unpolluted process waters may be discharged upon approval of the superintendent to a storm sewer or natural outlet. 
Sec. 18-80. - Pretreatment facilities. 
    Where necessary in the opinion of the superintendent, the owner shall provide at his expense such preliminary treatment as may be necessary to: 
(1)	Reduce the biochemical oxygen demand to three hundred (300) milligrams per liter and the suspended solids to three hundred fifty (350) milligrams per liter; 
(2)	Reduce objectionable characteristics or constituents to within the maximum limits provided for in section 18-78; or 
(3)	Control the quantities and rates of discharge of such water wastes.
Plans, specifications and any other pertinent information relating to proposed preliminary treatment facilities shall be submitted for the approval of the superintendent, and no construction of such facilities shall be commenced until the approval is obtained in writing. Where preliminary treatment facilities are provided for any waters or wastes, they shall be maintained continuously in satisfactory and effective operation by the owner at his expense. 
Sec. 18-81. - Control manhole. 
    When required by the superintendent, the owner of any property served by a building sewer carrying industrial wastes shall install a suitable control manhole in the building sewer to facilitate observation, sampling and measurement of the wastes. Such manhole, when required, shall be accessible and safely located, and shall be constructed in accordance with plans approved by the superintendent. The manhole shall be installed by the owner at his expense, and the owner at his expense shall maintain the same so the manhole shall be safe and accessible at all times. 
Sec. 18-82. - Standard for measurements, tests. 
    All measurements, tests and analyses of the characteristics of waters and wastes to which reference is made shall be determined in accordance with Standard Methods for the Examination of Water and Sewage, at the control manhole provided in section 18-81, or upon suitable samples taken at such control manhole. If no special manhole has been required, the control manhole shall be considered to be the nearest downstream manhole in the public sewer to the point at which the building sewer is connected. 
Sec. 18-83. - Special arrangements. 
    No statement contained in this article shall be construed as preventing any special agreement or arrangement between the city and any industrial concern whereby an industrial waste of unusual strength or character may be accepted by the city for treatment, subject to payment therefor by the industrial concern. 
Secs. 18-84-18-100. Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - OUTDOOR LANDSCAPE WATERING 

Sec. 18-101. - Restriction on outdoor watering of landscape. 
    Outdoor watering for purposes of planting, growing, managing, or maintaining ground cover, trees, shrubs, or other plants may occur only between the hours of 4:00 p.m. and 10:00 a.m.; provided, however, that this limitation shall not create any limitation upon the following outdoor water uses: 
(a)	Commercial raising, harvesting, or storing of crops; feeding, breeding, or managing livestock or poultry; the commercial production or storing of feed for use in the production of livestock, including, but not limited to, cattle, calves, swine, hogs, goats, sheep, and rabbits, or for use in the production of poultry, including, but not limited to, chickens, hens, ratites, and turkeys; producing plants, trees, fowl, or animals; or the commercial production of aquacultural, horticultural, dairy, livestock, poultry, eggs, and apiarian products or as otherwise defined in O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3; 
(b)	Capture and reuse of cooling system condensate or stormwater in compliance with applicable sections of the Hawkinsville Code of Ordinance and state guidelines; 
(c)	Reuse of gray water in compliance with O.C.G.A. § 31-3-5.2 and applicable local board of health regulations; 
(d)	Use of reclaimed waste water by a designated user from a system permitted by the Environmental Protection Division of the Georgia Department of Natural Resourses to provide reclaimed waste water; 
(e)	Watering personal food gardens;
(f)	Watering new and replanted plants, seed, or turf in landscapes, golf courses, or sports turf fields during installation and for a period of thirty (30) days immediately following the date of installation; 
(g)	Drip irrigation or irrigation using soaker hoses;
(h)	Hand watering with a hose with automatic cutoff or handheld container;
(i)	Use of water withdrawn from private water wells or surface water by an owner or operator of property if such well or surface water is on said property; 
(j)	Watering horticultural crops held for sale, resale, or installation;
(k)	Watering athletic fields, golf courses, or public turf grass recreational areas;
(l)	Installation, maintenance, or calibration of irrigation systems; or
(m)	Hydroseeding.
(Ord. No. 2010-6, 12-6-10)
Sec. 18-102. - Enforcement. 
(a)	No person shall use or allow the use of water in violation of the restrictions on outdoor water use contained in this article. 
(b)	The Pulaski County Sheriff's Department shall be the enforcement authority for this article. The city manager may also authorize other departments as may be deemed necessary to support enforcement. 
(Ord. No. 2010-6, 12-6-10)
Sec. 18-103. - Penalties. 
    A violation of any section in this article shall subject the violator to the maximum punishment provided under the City Charter. A separate offense shall be deemed committed on each day during which a violation occurs or continues. 
(Ord. No. 2010-6, 12-6-10)
APPENDIX A - UNIFIED LAND DEVELOPMENT REGULATIONS 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
DIVISION 1. - TITLE AND AUTHORITY 

Sec. 1.1.1. - Title. 
    This ordinance regulates the use of land, the location and use of buildings and other site improvements, and the construction of public facilities and private improvements related to the development of land. This ordinance shall be known as and may be cited as "The Unified Land Development Regulations." 
(Ord. of 5-10-96)
Sec. 1.1.2. - Authority. 
    This ordinance is adopted under authority of Article 9, Section 2, Paragraph 3 of the Constitution of the State of Georgia, and pursuant to the Zoning Procedures Law (O.C.G.A. § 36-66-1 et seq.) and other applicable laws enacted by the General Assembly. 
(Ord. of 5-10-96)
DIVISION 2. - ADOPTION 

Sec. 1.2.1. - Repeal of conflicting ordinances. 
    All conflicting ordinances or parts of ordinances are hereby repealed to the extent of their conflict. Where this ordinance and another overlap, whichever imposes the more stringent restrictions shall prevail. 
(Ord. of 5-10-96)
Sec. 1.2.2. - Severability. 
    If any section, subsection, sentence, clause, phrase or portion of this ordinance or any amendment thereto is for any reason held invalid or unconstitutional by any court of competent jurisdiction, such portion shall be deemed as a separate, distinct and independent provision and such holding shall not affect the validity of the remaining portions hereof. 
(Ord. of 5-10-96)
Sec. 1.2.3. - Effective date. 
    This ordinance shall take effect upon its adoption by the Board of Commissioners. 
(Ord. of 5-10-96)
DIVISION 3. - PURPOSE AND INTENT 

[Sec. 1.3.1. - Purpose and intent.] 
(a)	The purpose of these regulations is to promote the public health, safety, and general welfare; to promote the orderly and beneficial development and expansion of communities within the county; to provide adequate light and air; to provide adequate water, sewerage, and surface drainage; to prevent undesirable overcrowding of population; to secure safety from fire, panic and other dangers; to promote the orderly and desirable subdivision of land; to insure the orderly and desirable development of streets; to promote the orderly and desirable development of public utilities and services; to provide adequate and sufficient land for schools, parks, playgrounds, and other public uses; and to insure proper legal description and monumentation of all subdivided land. 
(b)	In the interpretation and application of this ordinance all provisions shall be:
(1)	Considered as minimum requirements;
(2)	Liberally construed in favor of the governing body; and,
